      <div class="page-header"> 
       <h2 itemprop="headline"> TTB | FAQs | Alcohol </h2> 
      </div> 
      <div itemprop="articleBody"> 
       <div id="bodymain">
        <script language="javascript"> 
var myBC = "<ul class='breadcrumb'><li><a href='https://www.ttb.gov'>TTB Home</a></li><li><a href='/faqs'>Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)</a></li><li>Alcohol FAQs</li></ul>"; 
</script> 
        <h1><a id="content" name="content"></a>Alcohol FAQs</h1> 
        <p><input id="userFindInputText" onfocus="clearMe()" name="userFindInputText" size="20" type="text" placeholder="Search">&nbsp;&nbsp;<input id="userFindInputButton" type="button" value="Search in Page">&nbsp;&nbsp;<span id="resText"></span>&nbsp;&nbsp;<input id="SAButton" onclick="showAll()" type="button" value="EXPAND ALL">&nbsp;&nbsp;<input id="HAButton" onclick="hideAll()" type="button" value="COLLAPSE ALL"></p> 
        <h2>By Commodity</h2> 
        <p><a title="Beer FAQs" href="/beer/beer-faqs" target="_self">Beer</a> | <a title="Distilled Spirits FAQs" href="/distilled-spirits/distilled-spirits-faqs" target="_self">Spirits</a> | <a href="/wine/wine-faqs">Wine</a></p> 
        <h2>Other Alcohol FAQs</h2> 
        <p align="center"><a href="#general">General Questions</a> | <a href="#Business">Business Questions</a> | <a href="#alfd">Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division</a> | <a href="#oa">Organic Alcohol</a> | <a href="#FMB">Flavored Malt Beverages</a> | <a title="Kombucha Information and Resources" href="/kombucha/kombucha-general" target="_self">Kombucha</a> | <a href="#caffeine">Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine</a> | <a href="#ecp">Export Certificate Program</a> | <a href="#sf">Serving Facts Statements</a> | <a href="#sug">Sugar Content Statements</a> | <a href="#af">Alcohol Facts Statements</a> | <a href="#EP">Extraction Products</a> | <a href="#Cider">Cider</a> | <a href="#hw">Honey Wine (Mead)</a> | <a href="#sch">Shelf Schematics</a> | <a href="#ND">Natural Disasters</a></p> 
        <h2>Related FAQs</h2> 
        <p><a href="/faqs/colas-and-formulas-online-faqs" target="_self">COLAs Online</a></p> 
        <p>&nbsp;</p> 
        <div id="contactFooter"> 
         <p><strong><img src="/images/phone.png" alt="Green icon with a white phone." width="29" height="29" align="absmiddle"> CONTACT US</strong><br> If you are concerned with the accuracy of this information, please <a href="/about-ttb/contact-us">contact TTB</a> or your legal advisor.</p> 
        </div> 
        <p>&nbsp;</p> 
        <div id="print_general" class="print_general">
         <a id="general" name="general"></a> 
         <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_general')" href="#general"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
         <h3>General Questions</h3> 
         <div id="Gmenu1" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g1" name="g1"></a>G1: Can I produce beer, wine or spirits for my personal or family use without paying <a href="/tax-audit/special-occupational-tax-and-fee-rate" target="_self">Federal excise tax</a> and filing Federal paperwork?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub1" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p><strong>Beer</strong></p> 
           <p><a href="/images/pdfs/25_205.htm" target="_blank">Production.</a></p> 
           <p><a href="/images/pdfs/25_206.htm" target="_blank">Removal of beer.</a></p> 
           <p><strong>Wine</strong></p> 
           <p><a href="http://edocket.access.gpo.gov/cfr_2006/aprqtr/27cfr24.75.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Wine for personal or family use.</a></p> 
           <p><strong>Spirits</strong></p> 
           <p>You cannot produce spirits for beverage purposes without paying taxes and without prior approval of paperwork to operate a distilled spirits plant. [See 26 U.S.C. <a href="http://uscode.house.gov/browse.xhtml" target="_blank" rel="noopener">5601</a> &amp; <a href="http://uscode.house.gov/browse.xhtml" target="_blank" rel="noopener">5602</a> for some of the criminal penalties. You should also review our <a href="/distilled-spirits/penalties-for-illegal-distilling" target="_self">Home Distilling</a> page.] There are numerous requirements that must be met that make it impractical to produce spirits for personal or beverage use. Some of these requirements are paying excise tax, filing an extensive <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=177fd53684cdbe612f989c4b34785695&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.4.159.2&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">application</a>, filing a <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=177fd53684cdbe612f989c4b34785695&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.6.166.1&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">bond</a>, providing adequate <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=177fd53684cdbe612f989c4b34785695&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.7.170.8&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">equipment</a> to measure spirits, providing suitable <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=2cb681631158b600029ec232d8f64c70&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.7.168.2&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">tanks</a> and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=b3882eaa61f957a6b10ef10af44a82e5&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.7.169.7&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">pipelines</a>, providing a <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=b3882eaa61f957a6b10ef10af44a82e5&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.3.157.2&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">separate building</a> (other than a dwelling) and maintaining detailed <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=e4710d90c1807b5d2d00c7396e2d13d4&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.22.220.10&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">records</a>, and filing <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=e4710d90c1807b5d2d00c7396e2d13d4&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.22.227.48&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">reports</a>. All of these requirements are listed in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=e4710d90c1807b5d2d00c7396e2d13d4&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR Part 19.</a></p> 
           <p>Spirits may be produced for nonbeverage purposes for fuel use only without payment of tax, but you also must file an <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=e4710d90c1807b5d2d00c7396e2d13d4&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.235.9&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">application,</a> receive TTB's <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=e4710d90c1807b5d2d00c7396e2d13d4&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.235.15&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">approval</a>, and follow requirements, such as <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=31fbab4968670ad7bd39e49dd7fbb8ec&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.240.33&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">construction</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=31fbab4968670ad7bd39e49dd7fbb8ec&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.246.49&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">use,</a> <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=31fbab4968670ad7bd39e49dd7fbb8ec&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.243.42&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">records</a> and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;SID=31fbab4968670ad7bd39e49dd7fbb8ec&amp;rgn=div8&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15.24.244.44&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">reports</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/06/2015</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu2" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g2" name="g2"></a>G2: What are the Federal and State excise taxes rates for spirits, wine and beer?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub2" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p><a href="/tax-audit/special-occupational-tax-and-fee-rate" target="_self"><strong>FEDERAL EXCISE TAX</strong></a></p> 
           <p><a href="/tax-audit/special-occupational-tax-and-fee-rate" target="_self">View</a> the Federal tax rates for wine, beer, and distilled spirits.</p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.taxadmin.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>STATE EXCISE TAX</strong></a></p> 
           <p>For information on the State taxes imposed on wine, beer, and distilled spirits, please visit <a href="http://www.taxadmin.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">www.TaxAdmin.org</a>, or contact the appropriate <a href="http://www.taxadmin.org/state-tax-agencies" target="_blank" rel="noopener">State tax or revenue agency</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 04/29/2010</span></p>

          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu3" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g3" name="g3"></a>G3: Who can I contact when I have a complaint or suspect illegal activity by a bar, club, liquor store, restaurant or other business selling beverage alcohol products (spirits, wine or beer)?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub3" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>With the exception of labeling, advertising and containers, the Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau does not enforce laws about selling or serving spirits, wine or beer to consumers. Usually, State governments regulate persons selling or serving spirits, wine or beer to consumers. This includes the minimum legal age that a person may sell or serve. Most States have commissions or agencies, which oversee persons and businesses that sell or serve beverage alcohol products. Contact the <a href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards" target="_self">appropriate State agency</a> for help in these areas. Also, visit the <a href="https://www.transportation.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Department of Transportation</a> website about restricting certain funds if a State allows the purchase or public possession of beverage alcohol products under the age of 21.</p> 
           <p>ACTIVITIES NOT RELATED TO BEVERAGE ALCOHOL PRODUCTS (spirits, wine or beer) - If you have information about illegal activities that do not involve beverage alcohol products (for example, drug sales or prostitution), report this information to the appropriate law enforcement agency. If you have information about illegal activities involving firearms, explosives, arson, or tobacco products, report this information to the <a href="https://www.atf.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives</a>.</p> 
           <p>LABELING, ADVERTISING OR CONTAINERS OF BEVERAGE ALCOHOL PRODUCTS (spirits, wine or beer) - Report this information to the Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau by <a href="mailto:alctobhq@ttb.treas.gov" target="_blank">e-mail</a>, <a href="/who-we-are/contact-us" target="_self">telephone</a> or writing to:</p> 
           <p><strong>Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau<br> Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division<br> 1310 G Street, NW., Box 12<br> Washington, DC 20005</strong></p> 
           <p>TRADE PRACTICES BETWEEN BUSINESSES SELLING OR PURCHASING BEVERAGE ALCOHOL PRODUCTS (spirits, wine or beer) - Report this information to the Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau at:</p> 
           <p><strong>Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau<br> Trade Investigations Division<br> 1310 G Street, NW., Box 12<br> Washington, DC 20005<br> Phone: 202-453-2271</strong></p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu4" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g4" name="g4"></a>G4: Does TTB have information or studies about the effects of consuming alcohol?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub4" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>The Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau does not normally conduct studies or maintain information about alcohol consumption because we do not enforce laws or regulations relating to the effects from consuming alcohol. The Bureau has <a href="/labeling/laws-and-regulations">regulations about labeling and advertising</a> and is committed to preventing consumer deception in beverage alcohol products.</p> 
           <p>There are several Federal web site addresses that may beneficial: <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/">https://www.whitehouse.gov</a>; <a href="https://www.hhs.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://www.hhs.gov/</a>; <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://www.samhsa.gov/</a>; <a href="https://www.justice.gov/">https://www.justice.gov/</a>; <a href="https://www.fhwa.dot.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://www.fhwa.dot.gov/</a> <a href="http://www.fhwa.dot.gov"></a>, and <a href="https://www.nhtsa.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"> https://www.nhtsa.gov/</a>.</p> 
           <p>You can also contact the <a href="https://www.niaaa.nih.gov/alcohol-health" target="_blank" rel="noopener">National Institute on Alcohol Abuse and Alcoholism</a>, 6000 Executive Blvd., Bethesda, MD 20892-7003 (301-443-3860).</p> 
           <p>Also, you may want to contact industry associations that represent beverage alcohol products industries. For example, from the Internet you should be able to reach the <a href="http://www.wineinstitute.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Wine Institute</a>, the <a href="http://www.discus.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Distilled Spirits Council of the United States</a>, and the <a href="http://www.beerinstitute.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Beer Institute</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div>

         <div id="Gmenu5" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g5" name="g5"></a>G5: How does TTB change its regulations?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub5" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Learn more about the rulemaking process at our <a href="/rrd/rulemaking-process">How Laws and Regulations are Made</a> page.</p>

         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu6" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g6" name="g6"></a>G6: Can a student make alcohol as part of a science fair project?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub6" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Well, under current law and regulations, we cannot allow you to conduct experiments involving distillation of alcohol at your home.</p> 
           <p>As an alternative, Federal law allows us to issue a permit for an alcohol fuel plant, or AFP. Under this type of permit, experiments with alcohol fuels can be conducted at locations properly qualified with TTB.</p> 
           <p>Here's what has to be done:</p> 
           <p>An authorized representative of your school (a teacher or other school official) must complete and forward an application form 5110.74 to us to establish a small AFP at your school.</p> 
           <p>The experiment must be conducted at your school under appropriate adult supervision.</p> 
           <p>The school official must tell us how long the experiment will last. They may allow for additional time in case your experiment is selected for additional competition or display at a regional or area science fair. And,</p> 
           <p>The school official must describe the adult supervision that will be provided. We require this because we are concerned about the safety of children handling hazardous materials and using distillation equipment with alcohol-even with adult supervision.</p> 
           <p>These steps apply primarily to students who are in elementary through high school. Make sure your application is filed as soon as possible to allow enough time for us to process it. You cannot begin the experiment until we issue you a permit.</p> 
           <p>Application form 5110.74 and additional information are available from the Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau, National Revenue Center, Spirits Unit A, 550 Main Street, Room 8002, Cincinnati, OH 45202-3263, 1-877-882-3277, or submit an <a href="/contact-nrc">online inquiry</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu7" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g7" name="g7"></a>G7: Are commercial vinegar producers regulated by TTB?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub7" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Yes. Many vinegar production methods include a stage where alcohol has developed but vinegar, with its distinctive sour taste, has not. TTB regulates commercial vinegar production when there is a potential Federal excise tax liability as beverage alcohol under 26 U.S.C. 5001, 5041, or 5051 at any stage of production, including on raw materials used to make the vinegar.</p> 
           <p>Finished vinegar is not subject to alcohol beverage excise tax for any one of the following reasons:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>the manufacturing process makes it unsuitable for beverage use;</li> 
            <li>the manufacturing process does not involve the production of alcohol; or</li> 
            <li>none of the ingredients used to make the vinegar are subject to excise tax.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>TTB does not regulate the following types of commercial vinegar production:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>vinegar made by diluting acetic acid;</li> 
            <li>wine vinegar made from purchased wine that was made unfit for beverage use by the producing winery; or</li> 
            <li>rice or malt vinegar made from purchased rice wine or beer that was made unfit for beverage use by the producing brewery.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>Generally, all other vinegar production methods are regulated by TTB.</p> 
           <p>The TTB requirements to produce various types of finished vinegar are discussed below. Our website contains <a href="/what-we-do/regs-guidance/regulations">links</a> to the TTB regulations cited on this page.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Wine vinegar</strong></p> 
           <p>The regulations covering wine and wine vinegar production are in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.19&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 24</a>  Wine.</p> 
           <p>If you make vinegar from fresh fruit or juice, (this type of vinegar is classified as nonbeverage wine) you must:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Qualify as a bonded wine cellar by filing an application and bond with TTB using <a href="/ponl/customer-support">Permits Online</a>. See <a href="/resources/business-central/industry-startup-tutorial" target="_blank">"Getting started in the Wine Industry"</a> for more information. If you make only vinegar, you will not need the Federal Alcohol Administration Act wine producer's permit that is required for producers of beverage wine.</li> 
            <li><a href="/formulation/customer-support">Obtain approval for your formula</a> indicating how you plan to make nonbeverage wine /vinegar.</li> 
            <li>Keep records and file reports in accordance with <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.19&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.19.15" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 24, subpart O</a>. You will not be subject to excise tax if you make only finished vinegar according to your approved formula.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>If you make vinegar from purchased beverage wine on which no tax has been paid, you must:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>File a bond (<a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f55102.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Form 5510.2</a>) with TTB to cover the tax on wine on hand, in transit, and unaccounted for until it is made into vinegar.</li> 
            <li>Purchase the wine in bond from a bonded wine cellar or winery.</li> 
            <li>In accordance with <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.19&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.19.14.346.17" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 24.291</a>, keep records of wine received, wine used in the manufacture of vinegar, vinegar produced, and vinegar removed, and allow examination of your premises by TTB officers.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>If you make vinegar from beverage wine on which the excise taxes are paid, TTB cannot refund the tax to you. Your operations will not be regulated by TTB.</p> 
           <p>If you make vinegar from wine that was made unfit for beverage use by the producing wine cellar or winery (therefore has no tax liability), then your operations are not regulated by TTB.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Malt or rice vinegar</strong></p> 
           <p>The regulations covering production of beer or rice wine (sak) are in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=e8c0de2472e6c2e31721e5572f8ed217&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 25</a>  Beer. Nonbeverage products made from beer or rice wine at breweries under approved formulas will not be subject to the Federal excise tax on beer when they are removed for sale.</p> 
           <p>If you produce your own beer or rice wine in the making of vinegar, you must:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Qualify with TTB as a brewer by filing a <a href="/beer/ttb-beer-brewers-notice">Brewer's Notice and bond</a> with TTB. In addition, you must obtain approval of the manufacturing of vinegar as an "other authorized use" of the brewery under <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=e8c0de2472e6c2e31721e5572f8ed217&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.20.3.371.3" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 25.23(b)</a> prior to production.</li> 
            <li><a href="/formulation/customer-support">Obtain approval of your formula</a> indicating how you plan to make nonbeverage beer or rice wine.</li> 
            <li>Keep records and file reports in accordance with <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=e8c0de2472e6c2e31721e5572f8ed217&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.20.21" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 25, subpart U</a>.</li> 
            <li>File tax returns, even when no tax is due (see <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=e8c0de2472e6c2e31721e5572f8ed217&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.20.11.382.11" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 25.164</a>).</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>If you purchase beer or rice wine that was made unfit for beverage use by the producing brewery, you may make that beer or rice wine into vinegar and your operations will not be regulated by TTB.</p> 
           <p>By law, beer or rice wine that is fit for beverage use cannot be transferred from the brewery to a manufacturer without payment of tax. If you make vinegar from beverage beer or rice wine on which the excise taxes are paid, TTB cannot refund the tax to you. Your operations will not be regulated by TTB.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Vinegar produced by distilling or the vaporizing process</strong></p> 
           <p>If you want to produce vinegar by the "vaporizing process" (a process that involves the distillation of alcohol), see our information on <a href="/applications/distilled-spirits-plant-dsp-industrial">qualifying as a distilled spirits plant</a> under <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR Part 19</a>. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.15&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.15.23" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 19 subpart W</a> for rules on production of vinegar by the vaporizing process.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Manufacturer of nonbeverage products (MNBP)</strong></p> 
           <p>If you buy taxpaid distilled spirits for vinegar production, TTB has a system for allowing drawback of most of the distilled spirits tax. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.13;idno=27;cc=ecfr" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 17</a> and <a href="/scientific-services-division/frequently-asked-questions">our frequently asked questions</a> to learn about the formula approval and claim process.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Vinegar production using specially denatured alcohol (SDA)</strong></p> 
           <p>"Specially denatured" alcohol is a distilled spirits product with certain materials added that make it unfit for beverage use, but suitable for industrial uses. These denatured alcohol products may be shipped free of tax to persons who hold TTB permits as industrial alcohol users. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.16;idno=27;cc=ecfr" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 20</a> and <a href="/images/pdfs/p51503.pdf" target="_blank">"Information for Specially Denatured Spirits Applicants"</a> for the permit, formula approval, and recordkeeping requirements for SDA users. Use <a href="/ponl/customer-support">Permits Online</a> to apply.</p> 
           <p>Three formulas of SDA are authorized as a raw material for vinegar production. In two of them (SDA formulas 29 and 35-A), the denaturant is ethyl acetate, and in the other (SDA formula 18), the denaturant is vinegar. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.17;idno=27;cc=ecfr#27:1.0.1.1.17.4.285.13">27 CFR 21.43</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.17;idno=27;cc=ecfr#27:1.0.1.1.17.4.285.26" target="_blank" rel="noopener">21.56</a>, and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.17;idno=27;cc=ecfr#27:1.0.1.1.17.4.285.32" target="_blank" rel="noopener">21.62</a> for the specific formulas. Commercial strength vinegar made from SDA may contain trace amounts of residual alcohol, not to exceed 0.5 percent alcohol by volume, in the finished product (<a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=0b1336cf26cbf0cd359ebd43d02b8706&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.16&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.16.7.278.10" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 20.104</a>).</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Labeling of vinegar</strong></p> 
           <p>Check with the <a href="https://www.fda.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Food and Drug Administration</a> for vinegar labeling rules.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>Other requirements</strong></p> 
           <p>Check with your <a href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards">State alcohol regulatory agency</a> to see if they regulate vinegar production.</p> 
           <p align="center"><strong>For more information</strong></p> 
           <p>If you have further questions, you may contact:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/offices/regulations-and-rulings-division">Regulations and Rulings Division</a> for general information;</li> 
            <li><a href="/offices/national-revenue-center">National Revenue Center</a> for information on the qualification process;</li> 
            <li><a href="/offices/alcohol-labeling-and-formulation-division">Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division</a> for information about formulas for nonbeverage products made at a winery or brewery; or</li> 
            <li><a href="/scientific-services-division/nonbeverage-products-laboratory-npl">Nonbeverage Products Laboratory</a> for nonbeverage products made by an MNBP or SDA user, and for advice concerning imported nonbeverage alcohol products.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu8" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g8" name="g8"></a>G8: Can I make vinegar for personal use?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub8" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>If you want to produce wine or malt vinegar for personal or family use and not for sale, the quantity may be included in the amount of wine or beer produced under the exemption in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.19&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.19.3.332.35" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 24.75</a> or <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=b127527c689bf67e7682a7cd3c269763;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.20;idno=27;cc=ecfr#27:1.0.1.1.20.12.390" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 25.205-207</a>. Please note that only a qualified distilled spirits plant may distill. There are no personal exemptions for production of distilled spirits.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu9" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g9" name="g9"></a>G9: Does TTB regulate butanols, such as isobutanol?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub9" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Isobutanol is a type of alcohol that may be produced from petroleum or by fermentation, and TTB requirements may apply depending on the circumstances. TTB's authority under the Internal Revenue Code (IRC) includes requirements relating to "distilled spirits." Under the IRC, this term includes ethyl alcohol in any form (e.g., beverage alcohol or fuel ethanol) except beer or wine. Although the term does not include isobutanol, TTB requirements apply if distilled spirits are produced or used in connection with isobutanol manufacturing. For example, if a manufacturer produces isobutanol by a fermentation process that also generates ethyl alcohol and the manufacturer separates the materials using distillation, the manufacturer may be required to qualify as a distilled spirits plant under 27 CFR part 19. For more information contact the <a href="/contact-rrd">Regulations and Rulings Division online</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu10" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g10" name="g10"></a>G10: Do I need a permit to import beverage alcohol products for my own use, or to ship or bring my personal alcohol collection into the U.S. from overseas?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub10" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Please visit TTB's <a href="/importers/personal-importation-of-alcohol-beverage-products">Personal Importation of Beverage Alcohol Products</a> page for information on bringing alcohol into the U.S. for non-commercial purposes.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed on July 16, 2020</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Gmenu11" class="mmenu">
          <a id="g11" name="g11"></a>G11: Can I import alcohol beverages (such as rum) made in Cuba into the United States?
         </div> 
         <div id="Gsub11" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p><span style="background-color: #ffffff;">The commercial importation into the United States of alcohol beverages made in Cuba is prohibited. Additionally, effective September 24, 2020, travelers returning to the United States may no longer bring back with them alcohol beverages of Cuban origin for personal use.</span>&nbsp;You may contact the <a href="https://home.treasury.gov/policy-issues/financial-sanctions/sanctions-programs-and-country-information" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Office of Foreign Assets Control</a> (OFAC) of the United States Department of the Treasury for additional information. See OFAC's Final Rule, "<a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2020/09/24/2020-21084/cuban-assets-control-regulations" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cuban Assets Control Regulations</a>" (September 24, 2020).</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 09/25/2020</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> <!--<div id="Gmenu12" class="mmenu">
			<a id="g12" name="g12"></a>G12: If authorized to travel to Cuba, or traveling in a third country, are there restrictions on the entities from whom I can purchase alcohol beverages or cigars made in Cuba?</div>
		<div id="Gsub12" class="subMenu">
			<div class="subs">
				<p>A: Yes. Alcohol beverages of Cuban origin, or cigars and other tobacco products of Cuban origin, cannot be purchased from a business included on the U.S. Department of State's list of restricted entities and sub-entities associated with Cuba. This list should therefore be reviewed prior to purchasing alcohol beverages of Cuban origin, or cigars and other tobacco products of Cuban origin. <a href="https://s3.amazonaws.com/public-inspection.federalregister.gov/2017-24449.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">See the U.S. Department of State's November 9, 2017 List of Entities and Sub-entities Associated with Cuba (Cuba Restricted List). </a></p>

        <div id="print_business" class="print_business">
         <a id="Business" name="Business"></a> 
         <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_business')" href="#Business"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
         <h3>Business Questions</h3> 
         <div id="BUmenu1" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu1" name="bu1"></a>BU1: What must I do if I want to start a business that sells or imports beverage alcohol products (spirits, wine, and beer)?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub1" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>While TTB does not regulate the licensing of persons who make retail sales of alcohol to consumers, retailers of alcohol beverages are required to file a registration form with TTB on <a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=904:5000-2&amp;catid=48" target="_self">TTB F 5630.5d</a> and to maintain certain <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=a0e25d4da42308ec77cd9c35340bfef3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.26&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.26.10.549" target="_blank" rel="noopener">records</a>. Retailers must file <a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=904:5000-2&amp;catid=48" target="_self">TTB F 5630.5d</a> when beginning sales of alcohol, whenever there are changes to the previous registration, and when the retail alcohol business is discontinued.</p> 
           <p>Persons who wish to wholesale (buying alcohol for sale to another wholesaler or to a retailer) or import alcohol beverages must obtain a permit from TTB before starting operations. Visit our <a href="/ponl/customer-support">Permits Online</a> homepage to learn more about applying for a wholesaler or importer permit. In addition, alcohol wholesalers and importers are required to submit a registration form on <a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=904:5000-2&amp;catid=48" target="_self">TTB F 5630.5d</a> and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=a0e25d4da42308ec77cd9c35340bfef3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.26&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.26.10.547" target="_blank" rel="noopener">keep records</a>. Read more information on <a href="/wholesaler">wholesaling and importing alcohol</a>.</p> 
           <p>Each State also regulates businesses that sell alcohol beverages. Alcohol businesses must comply with all State and local requirements in addition to the TTB requirements. See the <a href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards">list</a> of State alcohol regulatory agencies.</p> 
           <p>If you have additional questions, contact the National Revenue Center by phone at 1-877-882-3277 or <a href="/contact-nrc">online</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="BUmenu2" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu2" name="bu2"></a>BU2: What is required to sell beverage alcohol products (spirits, wine, or beer) on the Internet?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub2" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>The Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau (TTB) issued <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2000-1.htm">TTB Ruling 2000-1</a> concerning direct shipments and sales that includes sales transacted on the Internet. You are still subject to the same TTB requirements for selling spirits, wine, or beer. In addition, you also need to contact the appropriate <a href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards">State government agencies</a> where you and your purchaser are located. Ask whether you need licenses or permits and who needs to pay any taxes and what other requirements may apply. See our <a href="/publications/direct-shipping">Direct Shipping</a> Web page for more information.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="BUmenu3" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu3" name="bu3"></a>BU3: Can a business get back the tax money from alcohol or tobacco if the product is destroyed in a disaster such as a fire, earthquake, flood, or tornado?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub3" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Under certain circumstances, the tax money may be refunded for alcohol and tobacco products. See TTB Information sheet I 1200.68 (11-2004). Go to <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f56208.pdf" target="_blank">claim form</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="BUmenu4" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu4" name="bu4"></a>BU4: I do not run a bar or liquor store, but sometimes I include alcohol beverages with my product or service. Do I owe Special Occupational Tax (SOT) as a liquor dealer?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub4" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>No. There is no more Special Tax for periods beginning on or after July 1, 2005. However, if you failed to pay Special (Occupational) Tax for tax periods ending before or on June 30, 2005, you may be liable.</p> 
           <p>Retail liquor dealers must still keep records and register with TTB. Even though you do not run a bar or liquor store, we may consider you a retail liquor dealer if you conduct activities similar to the following examples:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Operate a limousine service and serve complimentary drinks to passengers,</li> 
            <li>Sell gift baskets that include wine, or</li> 
            <li>Run a bed-and-breakfast and serve complimentary drinks to guests in the afternoon.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>If you make a separate charge for the alcohol beverage (or if you charge different prices for your product or service with and without the alcohol beverage) you are definitely a retail liquor dealer.</p> 
           <p>If you have any state or local license that authorizes your business to sell beverage alcohol products, you are a retail liquor dealer.</p> 
           <p>Even if you do not make a separate charge or have a State or local liquor license, if the complimentary alcohol beverage is always included in the product or service, or if you advertise that your product or service includes a complimentary alcohol beverage, you are a retail liquor dealer. If an alcohol beverage is presented as "complimentary" to clients who pay for a particular product or service, we consider the cost as built into the charge for the product or service. If you provide alcohol beverages to most of your customers, but a particular customer declines to accept the alcohol beverage or if certain customers may not be lawfully served, we will still consider you to be engaged in the business of selling or offering beverage alcohol products for sale.</p> 
           <p>A true complimentary or gift situation, where a business that serves alcohol beverages is not considered a retail liquor dealer, is likely to be a rare situation.</p> 
           <p>If you have questions about whether your business is a retail liquor dealer, contact the TTB National Revenue Center at 1-877-882-3277. We will consider the nature of the business, the manner of operation and the advertising of the business to determine if the intent is to "sell" alcohol beverages.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="BUmenu5" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu5" name="bu5"></a> BU5: I want to open a business that sells beverage alcohol products at retail such as a bar, catering service or carryout, how do I get a license and will I owe any Federal Tax or Fees?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub5" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>If you sell beverage alcohol as part of your business, you must <a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=2583:repeal-sot&amp;catid=93">register</a> your business using <a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=904:5000-2&amp;catid=48" target="_self">TTB F 5630.5d</a>. Beverage alcohol means distilled spirits, wine, beer, mixed drinks, and beer or wine coolers.</p> 
           <p>Note: If you operated such a business prior to July 1, 2005, and did not pay Special (Occupational) Tax you may still be liable. This tax applied to persons who sold on or off premises or who provided alcoholic beverages as part of the cost of an item or service. You may have owed this tax even when you did not make a profit or when you were exempt from income tax. We have a <a href="/ttb-audiences/business-owners/retailers-beverage-alcohol">list of businesses</a> that may have been subject to this tax.</p> 
           <p><strong>The TTB does NOT issue a license to sell tobacco or beverage alcohol products at retail. You must contact your <a title="index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=2663:state-abc&amp;catid=99" href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards">State</a> or local licensing authority to obtain a retail license.</strong></p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="BUmenu6" class="mmenu">
          <a id="bu6" name="bu6"></a> BU6: I am planning to file an application with TTB for a permit or other approval to operate (such as a brewer's notice). Can I file the application although I'm not quite ready to open for business?
         </div> 
         <div id="BUsub6" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>You do not need to be ready to open your business at the time you file your application, but you must be able to provide all the information required for the application. Depending on the application type, required information may include a description of the premises and certain equipment you will use. Therefore, you should generally have construction complete and necessary equipment in place or on order. TTB publishes <a href="/nrc/statistics-original-applications-to-operate">average application processing times</a> to assist applicants in planning their operations, but the time necessary to process each application may vary.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/18/2017</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div>

        <div id="print_alfd" class="print_alfd">
         <a id="alfd" name="alfd"></a> 
         <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_alfd')" href="#alfd"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
         <h3>Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division</h3> 
         <div id="Amenu1" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf1" name="alf1"></a>A1: Questions and Answers for TTB Ruling on Caloric and Carbohydrate Representation in Alcohol Beverage labeling and Advertising.
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub1" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>See "Frequently Asked Questions: <a href="/rulings/rulings-faqs">TTB Ruling 2004-1"</a></p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu2" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf2" name="alf2"></a>A2: I live in one state and wish to send alcohol to my father in another state. May I send this package through the mail or does the distributor have to send the package?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub2" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>The U.S. Postal Service does not ship alcohol. Therefore, you will need to contact a private courier service such as FedEx or UPS to ship the alcohol. Also, contact the States to and from which you are shipping to find out if either has any laws or regulations prohibiting this practice.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu3" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf3" name="alf3"></a>A3: Does TTB charge a fee for label approval? If so, how much does it cost?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub3" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>You pay no fee either to obtain a copy of the form (<a href="/resources/faqs/alcohol?view=article&amp;id=904:5000-2&amp;catid=48" target="_self">TTB F 5100.31, Application for and Certification/Exemption of Label/Bottle Approval</a>) or to apply for label approval. If you are applying for label approval for the first time, you will need to send a copy of your approved basic permit or brewer's notice (depending on your business). You must also submit your application in duplicate with the labels attached to the front of the form. If your labels are too large to fit on the front of the form, you must reduce them and place the originals on the back of the form. Item no. 17 of the label application should reflect the percentage of reduction.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu4" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf4" name="alf4"></a>A4: As a student at the University of Kansas, I am researching why alcohol beverages do not have a nutritional value label as do all other foods, includingwater. I would like to know the calorie content and other information of my drink.
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub4" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>On August 10, 1993, the Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco and Firearms published an advanced notice of proposed rulemaking in the Federal Register that solicited comments from the public and industry on whether the regulations should be amended to require nutritional information on labels of alcohol beverages. The comment period for the ANPRM closed on February 7, 1994.</p> 
           <p>ATF received 55 comments in response to the advance notice. Only seven of these comments came from consumers. However, five of the seven consumers who commented opposed nutrition labeling. Overall, 80 percent of the comments received in response to the ANPRM opposed nutrition labeling for alcohol beverages. Thirty-five of the comments opposing nutrition labeling were submitted on behalf of industry, both domestic and foreign.</p> 
           <p>After careful consideration of the petition and the comments received in response to the advance notice, ATF determined that an amendment of the regulations to provide nutrition information on labels of alcohol beverages is unnecessary and unwarranted.</p> 
           <p>If you have a question about nutritional information on a particular product, you should contact the company by writing to the address on the label. Most companies will assist you if you ask them for this information.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu5" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf5" name="alf5"></a>A5: I am trying to determine what I need to do to make and sell a fermented apple cider with alcohol content under 7 percent by volume. The Food and Drug Administration claims that this falls entirely within their jurisdiction. Does TTB also regulate these products?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub5" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>The Food and Drug Administration has primary jurisdiction over the labeling of a fermented cider that contains less than 7 percent alcohol by volume. However, TTB has jurisdiction over some labeling requirements, most importantly the Government Warning Statement for any alcohol beverage over 0.5 percent alcohol by volume. These requirements are specified in 27 CFR part 16.</p> 
           <p>Most commercial fermented cider producers must register with TTB and pay tax on their cider. There is a very limited exemption from registration and tax requirements for "the non-effervescent product of the normal alcoholic fermentation of apple juice only, which is sold or offered for sale as cider and not as wine or as a substitute for wine." If the fermented cider you make does not fit that exemption, you must register with TTB as a bonded winery, pay tax and follow other rules for winery operation in TTB regulations at 27 CFR part 24, including TTB-enforced wine label requirements in 27 CFR  24.257.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/10/2010</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu6" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf6" name="alf6"></a>A6: How long does it take to get label approval?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub6" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>To help you with your planning process, we provide the current average COLA processing times for each commodity (wine, distilled spirits, and malt beverages) on our website at and through our Customer Service Call Center phone line. This gives you a quick and easy way to check the average number of days we are taking to respond to COLA applications.</p> 
           <p>You can access average COLA processing times:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>on our website on the <a href="/labeling/processing-times">labeling processing times</a> page, or</li> 
            <li>by phone at 202-453-2250 or toll free at 1-866-927-2533 to hear a recorded message: 
             <ul> 
              <li>press 4 for malt beverage and distilled spirits labels, and</li> 
              <li>press 6 for wine labels.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>You can always check the status of your application by logging into <a href="/labeling/colas">COLAs Online</a>.</p> 
           <p align="right">ALFD / revised June 2014</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p>

          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu7" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf7" name="alf7"></a>A7: Must I have a TTB permit before I can apply for label approval?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub7" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Yes, we must issue you a permit, brewer's notice or approval to operate a bonded wine cellar (BWC) or tax paid wine bottling house (TPWBH) before you submit an application for a certificate of label approval. You can apply for a permit online at <a href="/ponl/customer-support">Permits Online</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu8" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf8" name="alf8"></a>A8: How do I secure a TTB permit or a brewer's notice?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub8" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Our National Revenue Center in Cincinnati, Ohio, issues basic permits and brewer's notices. For information on obtaining a basic permit or brewer's notice see our <a href="/ponl/customer-support">Permits Online</a> webpage or contact the National Revenue Center at 1-877-882-3277.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/09/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu9" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf9" name="alf9"></a>A9: What does it mean when your labels are approved?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub9" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>A certificate of label approval authorizes the certificate holder to bottle and remove or import alcohol beverages that bear labels identical to those shown on the certificate of label approval.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p>

         <div id="Amenu10" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf10" name="alf10"></a>A10: We removed this FAQ because it was out-of-date.
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub10" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>None</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 11/30/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p>

         <div id="Amenu11" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf11" name="alf11"></a>A11: Can I request informal or preliminary comments from TTB on a proposed label?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub11" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Due to considerable increases in the number of label approval applications we receive and reductions in staffing, we no longer perform informal review of proposed labels. We offer a variety of resources on the <a href="/labeling">Labeling Home Page</a> to help you make sure your labels meet the regulatory requirements.</p> 
           <p align="right">ALFD / revised August 2011</p>

         <div id="Amenu12" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf12" name="alf12"></a>A12: If I am only adding my Internet Web site address to a label, do I need to get a new certificate of label approval?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub12" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>No. We authorize numerous changes that can be made to previously approved labels without applying for a new certificate of label approval (COLA), and the addition of an Internet address is one of the allowable revisions. The entire list of changes that may be made to approved labels without getting a new COLA is found on <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f510031.pdf" target="_blank">TTB F 5100.31, Application for and Certification/Exemption of Label/Bottle Approval</a>. For more information, please visit our <a href="/labeling/allowable-revisions">allowable revisions Web page</a>, or to view examples use our <a href="/allowable-revisions/allowable-changes-sample-label-generator">Allowable Changes Sample Label Generator</a>.</p>

         <div id="Amenu15" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf15" name="alf15"></a>A15: What is a Statement of Process?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub15" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>A Statement of Process is a formula for a domestically produced flavored malt beverage, flavored or unflavored rice wine, or sak. A statement of Process consists of 1) a detailed and specific quantitative list of each ingredient in the product and 2) a step-by-step description of the production process. As a minimum, a Statement of Process must include information on the volume and alcohol content of the malt beverage base, identification and source of any flavoring material used in the product, the maximum volume and alcohol content of each flavoring material used in the product, the percentage of alcohol contributed by the flavor(s) to the finished product, a specific description of when flavoring material is added in the production of the product, and the total volume and alcohol content of the finished product.</p> 
           <p>Statements of Process must be on brewery letterhead.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu16" class="mmenu">

           <p>If you want the flexibility to make changes to personalize your labels for customers without the need to submit new applications for each personalized label, you will need to follow the steps noted in public guidance document <a href="https://www.ttb.gov/public-guidance/2017-2-personalized-labels">TTB G 2017-2</a>, dated 9/5/17.</p>

         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu17" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf17" name="alf17"></a>A17: What are bioengineered foods?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub17" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Bioengineered foods are food or drink made from plant varieties that are developed from using recombinant deoxyribonucleic acid (rDNA) technology (which is often referred to as "genetic engineering" or "biotechnology"). Specifically, bioengineered foods are produced from plants whose genetic material has been altered by inserting DNA molecules from another organism for the purpose of reproducing beneficial characteristics, such as added nutrition, better flavor, or greater ability to fight pests or diseases, of the original species in the receiving species. In 1994, the Food and Drug Administration (FDA) established a consultation process that helps ensure that foods developed using biotechnology methods meet the applicable safety standards.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu18" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf18" name="alf18"></a>A18: Do bioengineered ingredients have any apparent health and safety risks when used in the production of alcohol beverages?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub18" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>There are no apparent health or safety risks associated with bioengineered foods used in the production of alcohol beverages. TTB has no basis for concluding that alcohol beverages produced from bioengineered ingredients differ from other alcohol beverages in any meaningful or uniform way, or that, as a class, alcohol beverages made from plant ingredients developed by the new techniques present any different or greater safety concern than alcohol beverages made from ingredients developed by traditional plant breeding.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu19" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf19" name="alf19"></a>A19: What is TTB's position with regard to the labeling statements about alcohol beverage products that are not bioengineered or that do not contain ingredients produced from bioengineered foods? For example, "Contains No GMOs," "GMO Free-Zone" or any similar references on alcohol beverages?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub19" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>Given the inquiries we have received and interest at the state level, we are reviewing our policy on the use of bioengineered food labeling statements or references on labels under our jurisdiction.</p>

         <div id="Amenu20" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf20" name="alf20"></a>A20: Am I permitted to label my product with a specialized farming term to show my compliance with or concern for environmental initiatives and movements?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub20" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>A description of specialized farming practices generally may appear on alcohol beverage labels as additional information provided it is truthful, accurate, specific, and does not conflict with, or in any manner qualify, mandatory labeling information. However, due to the constantly evolving nature of this field, TTB reserves the right to request clarification and documented verification of any graphics, seals, logos, definitions or language appearing on labels. For instance, any label specifically stating that the producer is certified by an agricultural organization must have documented proof.</p> 
           <p>Terms that refer to the environmental impact of the process and packaging rather than the product itself are usually acceptable. These words and phrases may not modify mandatory information on brand labels, but might appear as additional information after review on a case-by-case basis.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu21" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf21" name="alf21"></a>A21: What is required when applying for a certificate of exemption from label approval for my wine label instead of a Certificate of Label Approval on Form 5100.31?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub21" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>You may apply for a certificate of exemption from label approval for your wine only if it is produced or bottled in the United States and only if it will be sold, offered for sale, shipped, or delivered for shipment within the state in which it was bottled or packed (in other words, it will not be introduced into interstate commerce). This can be accomplished by selecting and completing item 18b on your label application, TTB Form 5100.31. Imported bottled wines are not eligible for a certificate of exemption from label approval and therefore must be covered by a Certificate of Label Approval.</p> 
           <p>Wines labeled under a certificate of exemption from label approval must show the statement, "For sale in _________(name of State) only." This statement may be added to a label covered by a certificate of exemption, or may be on an additional label that is affixed to the container. The statement does not have to appear on the label that is submitted to TTB, but must be on the container before it is removed from bond for consumption or sale.</p> 
           <p>Although the labeling requirements in 27 CFR Part 4, Labeling and Advertising of Wine, do not apply when a certificate of exemption is used, all of the rules in the wine regulations under the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 (IRC), 27 CFR Part 24, continue to apply to all wine bottled and packed in the United States. For example, 27 CFR 24.257(a) outlines what information must appear on your label, as well as the minimum type size requirements, for each bottle or other container of beverage wine prior to removal for consumption or sale. In brief, each label must contain:</p> 
           <ul type="disc"> 
            <li>Name &amp; Address of the wine premises where bottled or packed</li> 
            <li>Brand name if different from the above</li> 
            <li>Alcohol content as percent by volume or as stated in accordance with 27 CFR Part 4</li> 
            <li>The kind of wine</li> 
            <li>Net contents</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>Please see the complete text of 27 CFR 24.257 for additional information and guidance. (Note that Part 24 does not apply in Puerto Rico. See 27 CFR 24.2.)</p> 
           <p>The recordkeeping requirements in the IRC wine regulations continue to apply when a certificate of exemption is used. The wine regulations state in 27 CFR 24.257(b): "The information shown on any label applied to bottled or packed wine is subject to the recordkeeping requirements of [27 CFR 24.314, Label information record]," which states:</p> 
           <p>A proprietor who removes bottled or packed wine with information stated on the label (e.g., varietal, vintage, appellation of origin, analytical data, date of harvest) shall have complete records so that the information appearing on the label may be verified by an [sic] TTB audit. A wine is not entitled to have information stated on the label unless the information can be readily verified by a complete and accurate record trail from the beginning source material to removal of the wine for consumption or sale. All records necessary to verify wine label information are subject to the record retention requirements of  24.300(d).</p> 
           <p>In addition, Congress recently amended section 5388(c) of the IRC (26 U.S.C. 5388(c)) to restrict the use of certain wine names of European origin for wines sold in the United States. These wine names are: Burgundy, Claret, Chablis, Champagne, Chianti, Malaga, Marsala, Madeira, Moselle, Port, Rhine wine, Hock, Sauterne, Haut Sauterne, Sherry, Tokay and Retsina. These names may be used on labels for wine from the European Community (and made in accordance with the requirements of the Community) and on certain previously approved non-Community wine labels if their uses are grandfathered as of March 10, 2006. Because the IRC applies to wine regardless of whether it is in intrastate or interstate commerce, the restriction on the use of these names applies in both contexts. Accordingly, TTB will not issue a certificate of exemption for wine using one of these wine names in a manner not authorized by the statute. The change in the law was effective on December 20, 2006.</p> 
           <p>The Alcoholic Beverage Labeling Act of 1988, 27 U.S.C. 213 et seq., and implementing regulations in 27 CFR Part 16, which require a specified health warning statement on alcoholic beverages bottled or imported for sale or distribution in the United States, also apply equally to wine sold or shipped in intrastate or interstate commerce. Under Part 16, the required warning statement is a prerequisite for approval of a certificate of exemption from label approval, just as it is for a Certificate of Label Approval.</p> 
           <p>Finally, other laws may apply to fraudulent conduct used to sell mislabeled wine or to mislead consumers, including certain federal criminal statutes relating to fraud carried out through the use of: the mail; private or commercial interstate carriers; or wire, radio, or television communication in interstate or foreign commerce.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div>

         <div id="Amenu23" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf23" name="alf23"></a>A23: Questions and answers about third party representation in labeling and formulation matters.
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub23" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>TTB has recently noticed an increase in questions from industry members as to whether or not it is mandatory to use third-party representatives in order to receive label or formula approval, and if the Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division (ALFD) provides special assistance when such representatives are employed. TTB has created some FAQs in order to address these concerns.</p> 
           <h3>ALFD Third-party Representation FAQs</h3> 
           <p>CS 1. What is a third-party representative? A third-party representative is a person or firm retained by an industry member in order to provide specific services for the member in dealing with TTB. In the label/formula approval area these services range from simple submission and return of an application via the Public Room in order to bypass any mail-room delays, to negotiations over areas of the label/formula that ALFD feels are in need of correction.</p> 
           <p>CS 2. Do I need a third-party representative? No. TTB provides the same level of service to third-party representatives as is provided to those who choose to work with TTB directly, but you may use a third-party representative if you so choose. ALFD Customer Service representatives will work directly with all industry members and representatives to answer label/formula questions and solve problems in a timely and accurate manner. See our <a href="/who-we-are/contact-us">hours for the Public Room</a> or contact ALFD at 866-927-2533 (toll free) or 202-453-2250 and select the appropriate option to schedule an appointment.</p> 
           <p>CS 3. Do I need to obtain a third-party representative in order to request Expedited or Temporary Approval? No. TTB will work directly with the industry member or a representative. However; all requests to expedite a label application or temporary label approvals are reviewed on a case-by-case basis and require supporting documentation. All inquiries should be made directly to Customer Service at 866-927-2533.</p> 
           <p>CS 4. Does TTB charge a fee for each label and formula application submitted? No. All labeling, formulation and advertising services provided to you by TTB are free of charge.</p> 
           <p>CS 5. Can I use a third-party representative? Yes, TTB will work with a third-party representative if you choose to retain one. However, obtaining a third-party representative is completely voluntary.</p> 
           <p>CS 6. How do I contact ALFD?</p> 
           <p>For questions on alcohol Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division you may contact ALFD directly online or by phone at:</p> 
           <p><strong>Online</strong>: <a href="/contact-alfd">Submit an Online Inquiry</a> <br><strong>Phone: 202-453-2250 or (toll-free) 866-927-2533<br> Option 1 = General information<br> Option 2 = Colas Online Password Resets <br> Option 3 = Colas Online Registration<br> Option 4 = Distilled Spirits/Malt Beverage Labeling and all Formulation<br> Option 5 = Alcohol Advertising<br> Option 6 = Wine Labeling</strong></p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div>

         <div id="Amenu25" class="mmenu">
          <a id="alf24" name="alf25"></a>A25: I operate a domestic winery and I am making wine from grapes or juice that I have purchased from another state or country. What appellation of origin may I use?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub25" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>This is a complicated question, and the answer (see <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.2&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.2.3.25.6" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 4.25(b))</a> depends on the particular circumstances. State or local laws and regulations may be more restrictive than Federal laws and regulations in some instances, and, to use an appellation, the wine must conform to the laws and regulations of the named appellation area. (Please note that we use here certain states or regions only as examples to illustrate certain different circumstances.) We advise that you confer with state and local authorities regarding their requirements before finalizing your COLA submission. Remember that your wine, and the records that you keep, must adequately support any claims which are made on your label. The following situations serve as examples. There are certainly more factual circumstances that might have a different outcome.</p> 
           <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Situation 1: I am making a wine with grapes or juice originating from a state that is contiguous to (that is, touching) my own state (e.g. when California grapes are used to produce wine in Oregon).</span>Suppose that I have purchased Napa Valley, California, grapes that I will produce into wine in Oregon.</p> 
           <p>The most specific appellation of origin eligible for use is the name of the contiguous state (California). A viticultural area appellation of origin (e.g. Napa Valley) may NOT be used because the wine was not fully finished within that state.</p> 
           <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Situation 2: The state from which the winemaking material originates is not contiguous to the state in which the wine is produced. For example, California grapes have been purchased to produce wine in New York.</span></p> 
           <p>The most specific appellation of origin eligible - for use is a country appellation, such as "American." Note that when a country is used as an appellation of origin a vintage date is NOT permissible for the wine.</p> 
           <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Situation 3: I am purchasing grapes or juice from another country.</span> An appellation of origin may NOT be used, as this wine is not eligible for such claims (see <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.2&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.2.3.25.6" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 4.25(b)(2)(ii))</a>. A vintage date or a varietal designation (e.g. Merlot) may not appear on the wine, as both items require an appellation of origin present on the label. The wine may be labeled only with a more general class or type statement, such as "Red Wine" or "White Wine."</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div>
