         <div id="Amenu27" class="mmenu">
          <a id="a27" name="a27"></a>A27: Does my TTB certificate of label approval mean I have trademark protection?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub27" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>TTB's authority to issue certificates of label approval (COLAs) for alcohol beverage products does not include trademark protection, as is stated in the instructions for <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f510031.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Form 5100.31</a>, Application for and Certification/Exemption of Label/Bottle Approval. While TTB may be aware of an established trademark when acting on an application for a COLA, that awareness is important only for carrying out the labeling authority under the deception and misleading standards imposed by the Federal Alcohol Administration Act and not for purposes of Federal law applicable to trademarks. Therefore, TTB approval of a COLA neither automatically confers trademark protection, nor indicates that a particular mark may be used in violation of applicable intellectual property law.</p> 
           <p>The U.S. Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO) provides for trademark registrations and guides United States domestic and international intellectual property policies. The USPTO website address is <a href="http://www.uspto.gov/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">www.uspto.gov/</a>. You may find the USPTO's list of frequently asked questions on the subject of trademarks particularly helpful: <a href="http://www.uspto.gov/faq/trademarks.jsp" target="_blank" rel="noopener">www.uspto.gov/faq/trademarks.jsp</a>. The USPTO also has a website on trademark protection specifically designed for small business owners at <a href="http://www.uspto.gov/smallbusiness/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">www.uspto.gov/smallbusiness/</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu28" class="mmenu">
          <a id="a28" name="a28"></a>A28: I would like to use social media to inform consumers where to find my products or promote a special event at a restaurant or retailer. Are there any restrictions on this?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub28" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>As we stated in <a href="/images/industry_circulars/archives/2013/13-01.html" target="_blank">TTB Industry Circular 2013-01</a>, TTB considers advertising in social media to be subject to all of the same requirements and restrictions as any other type of advertising under the Federal Alcohol Administration Act (FAA Act) and the TTB implementing regulations (<a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=506cf0c03546efff958847134c5527d3&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.2&amp;idno=27#sp27.1.4.g" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 4 subpart G</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=0b1336cf26cbf0cd359ebd43d02b8706&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.3&amp;idno=27#sp27.1.5.h">27 CFR part 5 subpart H</a>, and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=8838ac3aff1edbce8f3d3ba6724cf799&amp;mc=true&amp;node=sp27.1.7.f&amp;rgn=div6" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 7 subpart F</a>, and the tied house regulations at <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=bd9fafc114d17633cd17d16675654083;rgn=div5;view=text;node=27%3A1.0.1.1.4;idno=27;cc=ecfr" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR part 6</a>).</p> 
           <p>The regulations in parts 4, 5 and 7 require certain mandatory statements (e.g., responsible advertiser name and address) to appear in advertisements for wines, distilled spirits, and malt beverages, respectively. The regulations also prohibit certain advertising practices and statements from appearing in such advertisements.</p> 
           <p>Under the tied house regulations in part 6, industry members may not induce a retailer, directly or indirectly, to purchase alcoholic beverages from the industry member to the exclusion of such products offered for sale by other persons.&nbsp; We consider the listing of a retailer in an industry members advertisement, including a social media ad, to be providing a thing of value that constitutes a means to induce that retailer to purchase alcoholic beverages from that industry member. As such, listing a retailer in advertising, including social media advertising, may be a violation of the FAA Act if it results in exclusion as described in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/retrieveECFR?gp=&amp;SID=0668ea0ce942080930b4464ee0fd240f&amp;mc=true&amp;n=sp27.1.6.e&amp;r=SUBPART&amp;ty=HTML" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 6.151 through 6.153</a>, subject to the jurisdictional limits at <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=0668ea0ce942080930b4464ee0fd240f&amp;mc=true&amp;node=se27.1.6_14&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 6.4.</a>&nbsp;</p> 
           <p>An exception in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=0668ea0ce942080930b4464ee0fd240f&amp;mc=true&amp;node=se27.1.6_198&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 6.98</a> provides that listing the names and addresses of <em>two or more unaffiliated retailers</em> selling the products of an industry member does not constitute a means to induce. The requirements of the exception are that:</p> 
           <ol type="a"> 
            <li>The advertisement does not also contain the retail price of the product (except where the exclusive retailer in the jurisdiction is a State or a political subdivision of a State), and</li> 
            <li>The listing is the only reference to the retailers in the advertisement and is relatively inconspicuous in relation to the advertisement as a whole, and</li> 
            <li>The advertisement does not refer only to one retailer or only to retail establishments controlled directly or indirectly by the same retailer, except where the retailer is an agency of a State or a political subdivision of a State.</li> 
           </ol> 
           <p>State laws also apply, and they vary from state to state. We encourage industry members to contact the applicable state alcohol beverage authorities with any questions related to state law. Please see our website for a list of <a href="/wine/alcohol-beverage-control-boards">State Alcohol Beverage Authorities</a>.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/12/2016</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div id="Amenu29" class="mmenu">
          <a id="a29" name="a29"></a>A29: Will TTB approve any formulas or labels for alcohol beverage products that contain a controlled substance under Federal law, including marijuana?
         </div> 
         <div id="Asub29" class="subMenu"> 
          <div class="subs"> 
           <p>TTB will not approve any formulas or labels for alcohol beverage products that contain a controlled substance under Federal law, including marijuana. The Controlled Substances Act (CSA), 21 U.S.C.  802(16), defines marijuana as all parts of the <em>Cannabis sativa </em>L. plant (and its derivatives) with certain specific exclusions. Substances (such as tetrahydrocannabinols (THC), cannabidiols (CBD), or terpenes) that are derived from any part of the cannabis plant that is <em>not excluded </em>from the CSA definition of marijuana are controlled substances, regardless of whether such substances are lawful under State law. <em>See </em>Drug Enforcement Administration (DEA), <a href="https://www.deadiversion.usdoj.gov/schedules/marijuana/m_extract_7350.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Clarification of the New Drug Code (7350) for Marijuana Extract</a> for more information about DEA's position on cannabis derivatives. The parts of the cannabis plant that <em>are</em> excluded from the definition of marijuana in the CSA (referred to here as "hemp" ingredients) include hemp seed oil, sterilized hemp seeds, and non-resinous, mature hemp stalks.</p> 
           <p>Formula approval from TTB is required before a hemp ingredient may be used in the production of an alcohol beverage product. In determining whether a hemp ingredient is allowable for use in an alcohol beverage, TTB will consult with the DEA where appropriate and defers to the DEA in its interpretation of the CSA.</p> 
           <p>TTB also consults with the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) on ingredient safety issues where appropriate. In some cases, TTB may require formula applicants to obtain documentation from FDA indicating that the proposed use of an ingredient in an alcohol beverage would not violate the Federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act.</p> 
           <p>For alcohol beverage products containing a hemp ingredient, the product label must accurately and specifically identify the ingredient in a manner that makes it clear that the ingredient is not a controlled substance (e.g., "hemp seed oil" rather than "hemp oil"). Additionally, labeling statements for alcohol beverage products may not create the misleading impression that the product contains a controlled substance or has effects similar to those of a controlled substance.</p> 
           <p>For more information, including requirements for lab analysis of hemp components, please refer to the "<a href="/formulation/hemp-policy">Hemp Policy</a>" published by our predecessor agency in 2000.</p> 
           <p>TTB notes that section 7606 of the Agricultural Act of 2014, commonly referred to as the Farm Bill, defines "industrial hemp." <em>See </em>7 U.S.C. 5940.&nbsp; Subject to certain restrictions, this law allows an institution of higher education or a State department of agriculture to grow or cultivate industrial hemp for purposes of research where allowed under State law. As explained by the <em>Statement of Principles on Industrial Hemp </em>which was issued by USDA, in consultation with DEA and FDA, and published in the Federal Register on August 12, 2016, section 7606 does not authorize the sale of industrial hemp "for the purpose of general commercial activity." Accordingly, it is TTB's understanding that the Farm Bill does not authorize the use of industrial hemp in the production of alcohol beverage products for sale beyond limited State-sanctioned pilot projects by authorized entities.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/23/2018</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top </a></p> 
         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_oa" class="print_oa">
          <a id="oa" name="oa"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_oa')" href="#oa"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Organic Alcohol</h3> 
          <div id="OAmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa1" name="oa1"></a>OA 1: How do the USDA organic regulations apply to alcohol beverages?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The U.S. Department of Agriculture (USDA) organic regulations create standards for the production, handling, processing, labeling, and marketing of all organically produced agricultural products. The regulations also create four labeling categories and identify specific substances that cannot be used in the production of organically made products. To obtain more information about the National Organic Program and to view a full text of the regulations, please visit the National Organic Program Web site at <a href="https://www.ams.usda.gov/nop" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://www.ams.usda.gov/nop</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa2" name="oa2"></a>OA 2: What is an Organic Claim?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>If a bottler or importer uses the word "Organic" in any fashion likely to be perceived as claiming that a product or anything associated with it is organically produced, contains organic ingredients, or was processed in an organic manner or facility, TTB will consider this an organic claim and apply the requirements of the USDA organic regulations at 7 CFR part 205.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa3" name="oa3"></a>OA 3: What type of Organic Claims Exist?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The four labeling categories of the USDA organic regulations are as follows (with information pertinent to alcohol beverages):</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li><strong>"100% Organic"</strong> contains only organic ingredients and processing aids with no chemically added sulfites.</li> 
             <li><strong>"Organic"</strong> contains at least 95% organic ingredients with no chemically added sulfites.</li> 
             <li><strong>"Made with Organic [Ingredients]"</strong> contains at least 70% organic ingredients and may contain up to 100 ppm of sulfites from sulfur dioxide.</li> 
             <li>Products containing <strong>less than 70% organic ingredients</strong> and products that are not processed by a certified organic handling operation may only identify each organically produced ingredient in an ingredient statement.</li> 
            </ul> The complete USDA organic composition and labeling requirements are fully described in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=dc477c2b8a60aa3e6e805c66e74f7d38&amp;node=7:3.1.1.9.32.4&amp;rgn=div6" target="_blank" rel="noopener">7 CFR Subpart DLabels, Labeling and Market Information</a>. 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa4" name="oa4"></a>OA 4: When I submit a label application for a label with an organic reference, what additional documentation must I submit?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The information required depends on the circumstances. A majority of claims will require you to submit the <a href="https://www.ams.usda.gov/AMSv1.0/ams.fetchTemplateData.do?template=TemplateJ&amp;leftNav=NationalOrganicProgram&amp;page=NOPACAs&amp;description=USDA%2520Accredited%2520Certifying%2520Agents" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Certifier/Accredited Certifying Agent (ACA) Preview. </a></p> 
            <ul style="list-style: none;"> 
             <li>A. &nbsp;For "100% organic" "organic" and "made with organic [ingredients]:</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Certifier/ACA Preview</strong></span>  indicates that an Accredited Certifying Agent (ACA) has reviewed the applicant's label, reconciled it with the applicant's certification, and found the label to be in compliance with USDA organic regulations. The certifier/ACA Preview will show actual images of the labels along with a stamp or signature of the ACA.</p> 
            <ul style="list-style: none;"> 
             <li>B. &nbsp;For organic Ingredient statements:</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Producer's/Crop Organic Certificate</strong></span> - certifies that the grapes, fruit, or other agricultural produce used in the product comply with the USDA organic regulations. A list of different grapes, fruits, crops, and the year of harvest may appear on the actual certificate or on an attached addendum.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa5" name="oa5"></a>OA 5: My imported wine has organic documentation from the European Union/European Commission; will this documentation be sufficient to support my organic claim?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The United States has an organic equivalence arrangement with the European Union (EU). Under the terms of this arrangement, wine imported from the EU with organic labeling must comply with the labeling requirements of the USDA organic regulations.</p> 
            <p>For wine labeled organic, an EU control body must verify that prohibited substances, such as sulfur dioxide or potassium metabisulphite, were not added to the wine. For wine labeled made from organic grapes, an EU control body must ensure that no prohibited substances are used, except there is an allowance for the use of sulfur dioxide. The EU control body must verify that the total sulfite concentration from sulfur dioxide does not exceed 100 parts per million. Nonagricultural substances <span style="text-decoration: underline;">not</span> listed under 7 CFR 205.605 are prohibited in wine labeled organic or made with organic grapes.</p> 
            <p>The certifier/ACA preview must be submitted to TTB; this indicates that the EU control body has verified compliance with these terms of the EU-U.S. organic equivalence arrangement.</p> Organic certificate(s) submitted to TTB (if required- see Question 4) must be in English or have complete translation(s) attached. 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu6" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa6" name="oa6"></a>OA 6: What is a certifier/ACA Preview?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Certifiers/ACAs are private, State, and foreign entities accredited by the USDA for certifying foreign and domestic organic crop, livestock, and handling operations to USDA organic standards. All labeling applicants that are certified organic handlers and intend to make an organic claim (other than in an ingredient statement) on an alcohol beverage must submit the label(s) to their certifier/ACA for review and approval prior to submission to TTB. The certifier/ACA Preview is a document that must show actual images of the exact labels along with a stamp or signature of the certifier/ACA to verify that the product label complies with the USDA organic regulations. The National Organic Program maintains a list of Accredited Certifying Agents on its Web site at: <a href="https://www.ams.usda.gov/services/organic-certification/certifying-agents" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://www.ams.usda.gov/services/organic-certification/certifying-agents</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu7" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa7" name="oa7"></a>OA 7: Where do I obtain the certifier/ACA Preview for organic imported products?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The producers/handlers of alcohol products that will be imported into the United States are responsible for supplying copies of the required documents to the importer. The importer should request the documents from the handler or the producer's wholesale distributer for submission with your Certificate of Label Approval application.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu8" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa8" name="oa8"></a>OA 8: What documents must be provided if I want to state, "Made with Organically Grown [Ingredients]?"
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>To use "Made with Organically Grown [Ingredients]" on a label, you must submit a certifier/ACA preview.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu9" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa9" name="oa9"></a>OA 9: What else must I know if I want to state, "Made with Organically Grown Grapes?"
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub9" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <ul> 
             <li>The USDA organic seal, or foreign equivalent, is not allowed.</li> 
             <li>Use of non-organic grapes is not permitted.</li> 
             <li>Sulfur dioxide is the only sulfiting agent allowed; total sulfite concentration must not exceed 100 ppm. Sulfite disclosure is required on the label.</li> 
             <li>The disclosure of organic ingredients on the label must be in the form of a phrase such as "Made with Organic [specify your organic ingredients here]. Examples are: "Made with Organically Grown Grapes," "Made with Organic Grapes," "Made with Organic Grapes from Our Vineyard," or "Made with Organically Produced Grapes."</li> 
             <li>A Certification Statement Certified Organic by--- or a similar phrase must appear below the bottler or importer's name and address statement.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu10" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa10" name="oa10"></a>OA 10: What is a "Certification Statement," and where must it go on a label?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub10" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The statement, "Certified Organic by---" or a similar phrase followed by the name of the certifier/ACA must appear below the bottler or importer's name and address statement. The organic certification statement must appear under the importer's name and address on imported products if the foreign producer/bottler's information is not present. We will accept the certification statement beneath either the importer or the foreign producer/bottler's information when present on imported labels. The business address, Internet address, or telephone number of the certifying agent may be included on the label. Certifier/ACA acronyms are acceptable in certification statements; however, logos or seals alone do not fulfill this requirement.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu11" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa11" name="oa11"></a>OA 11: I have an organic crop certificate, but the producer is not a certified organic handler. What type of organic claim can be made on the label?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub11" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The only organic claim that can be made on the label is in an ingredient statement to indicate which ingredients are organic. If the organically produced ingredients are identified in the ingredient statement, the product's percentage of organic contents may be displayed on the information panel (7 CFR  205.305). Acceptable variations include "X% Organic" or "X% Organic ingredients."</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu12" class="mmenu">
           OA 12: If the vintage date changes on my approved organic label, do I need to submit a new application?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub12" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No, the vintage date may change on an organic label without obtaining a new Certificate of Label Approval.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu13" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa13" name="oa13"></a>OA 13: What are some common mistakes made when submitting organic labels?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub13" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The lack of supporting documentation for organic claims creates the greatest delay in label processing. In a majority of situations, the certifier/ACA preview will satisfy the requirement. A second common mistake occurs when submitters do not closely check the supporting documents to ensure that information listed on the product corresponds to the associated paperwork. Expired documentation, documents citing the incorrect product, and date conflicts represent common reasons why applications are returned.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="OAmenu14" class="mmenu">
           <a id="oa14" name="oa14"></a>OA 14: Aside from terms using the word "Organic," am I permitted to label my product with a specialized farming term to show my compliance with or concern for environmental initiatives and movements?
          </div> 
          <div id="OAsub14" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>A description of specialized farming practices generally may appear on alcohol beverage labels as additional information provided it is truthful, accurate, specific, and does not conflict with, or in any manner qualify, mandatory labeling information. However, due to the constantly evolving nature of this field, TTB reserves the right to request clarification and documented verification of any graphics, seals, logos, definitions, or language appearing on labels. For instance, any label specifically stating that the producer is certified by an agricultural organization must have documented proof.</p> 
            <p>Terms that refer to the environmental impact of the process and packaging rather than the product itself are usually acceptable. These words and phrases may not modify mandatory information on brand labels, but might appear as additional information after review on a case-by-case basis.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/12/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top </a></p> 
         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_sot" class="print_sot">
          <a id="FMB" name="FMB"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_sot')" href="#FMB"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Flavored Malt Beverage and Related Regulatory Amendments</h3> 
          <div id="FMBmenu1" class="mmenu">
           FMB1: <a id="Q1" name="Q1"></a> How does TTB TD-21 impact the composition of flavored malt beverages?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The new regulation permits the addition of flavors and other nonbeverage materials containing alcohol to beers and malt beverages. Malt beverages that contain not more than 6% alcohol by volume may derive no more than 49% of their alcohol content from flavors and other nonbeverage materials. If a malt beverage contains more than 6% alcohol by volume, not more than 1.5% of the volume of the finished product may consist of alcohol derived from flavors and other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu2" class="mmenu">
           FMB2 <a id="Q2" name="Q2"></a>: When do these new standards go into effect?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The final rule takes effect on January 3, 2006.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu3" class="mmenu">
           FMB3 <a id="Q3" name="Q3"></a>: My brewery produces a flavored malt beverage that derives over 90% of its alcohol content from added nonbeverage flavors, and only 10% of its alcohol content from fermentation at the brewery. What can we do if we want to continue to make this product on and after January 3, 2006?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>On and after January 3, 2006, a product that does not comply with the requirements of TTB TD-21 may not be produced at a brewery, bottled at a brewery, removed from a brewery with or without payment of tax, removed from customs custody for consumption, or (in the case of products not destined for exportation), transferred to a second customs bonded warehouse.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 04/15/2015</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu4" class="mmenu">
           FMB4 <a id="Q4" name="Q4"></a>: Does the final rule apply to imported as well as domestic malt beverages?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes.</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu5" class="mmenu">
           FMB5 <a id="Q5" name="Q5"></a>: The rule requires mandatory alcohol content labeling for flavored malt beverages. My brewery produces a fruit-flavored ale that derives 0.4% of its alcohol content from an added flavor. Do we need to label this ale with an alcohol content statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. The final rule requires an alcohol content statement on the label of any malt beverage that contains any alcohol derived from added flavors or other added nonbeverage ingredients (other than hop extract) containing alcohol.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu6" class="mmenu">
           FMB6 <a id="Q6" name="Q6"></a>: May I place the mandatory alcohol content statement on the back label?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. The mandatory alcohol content statement must appear on the brand label.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu7" class="mmenu">
           FMB7 <a id="Q7" name="Q7"></a>: My brewery produces a malt beverage made with a hop extract that adds a very minimal amount of alcohol to the product. Do we have to label this malt beverage with an alcohol content statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>As long as the malt beverage does not derive alcohol from any other added flavor or other added nonbeverage ingredient, it does not have to be labeled with an alcohol content statement.</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu8" class="mmenu">
           FMB8 <a id="Q8" name="Q8"></a>: If I ship my beer to another state, and that state has different labeling requirements, am I required to comply with those labeling requirements?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You are required to comply with the labeling laws of any state in which [or "where"] you sell your malt beverages. The labeling requirements of Title 27 <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=0e0d6143502cbb948d782dbd368dd81a&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.5&amp;rgn=div5" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Part 7</a> of our regulations apply only to the extent that State law imposes similar requirements on malt beverages sold within the State.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu9" class="mmenu">
           FMB9 <a id="Q9" name="Q9"></a>: The only change that my brewery must make to the label is to add the required alcohol content statement. Are we required to file a new application for label approval, or should we simply add the alcohol content statement to the label?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub9" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Your company may add an alcohol content statement to the label without applying for a new certificate of label approval.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu10" class="mmenu">
           FMB10 <a id="Q10" name="Q10"></a>: What new labeling and advertising provisions have been added to the regulations?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub10" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Consistent with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2002-2.htm">ATF Ruling 2002-2</a>, the final rule prohibits the use of labeling or advertising statements, designs, devices, or representations that tend to create a false or misleading impression that a malt beverage contains distilled spirits or is a distilled spirits product.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu11" class="mmenu">
           FMB11 <a id="Q11" name="Q11"></a>: My brewery's flavored malt beverage is labeled with a brand name that is also the brand name of a well-known distilled spirits product. Does TTB TD-21 allow this labeling practice?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub11" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The final rule provides that the use of a brand name of a distilled spirits product as the brand name of a malt beverage is not prohibited, provided that the overall label or advertisement does not present a misleading impression about the identity of the product.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu12" class="mmenu">
           FMB12 <a id="Q12" name="Q12"></a>: Does the final rule allow the use of cocktail names on FMB labels?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub12" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The final rule permits the use of a cocktail name as the brand name or fanciful name of a malt beverage, provided that the overall label or advertisement does not present a misleading impression about the identity of the product.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu13" class="mmenu">
           FMB13 <a id="Q13" name="Q13"></a>: How have the statement of process requirements changed?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub13" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Current regulations require brewers to file a statement of process whenever they propose to produce and market a fermented beverage under a name other than "beer," "ale," "porter," "stout," "lager," or "malt liquor." Under the new regulations, brewers will be required to file formulas (instead of statements of process) under the circumstances set forth in the regulations.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu14" class="mmenu">
           FMB14 <a id="Q14" name="Q14"></a>: What brewing processes will trigger the formula requirement?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub14" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Formulas will be required whenever the brewer intends to produce a fermented product that will be treated by any processing, filtration, or other method of manufacture that is not generally recognized as a traditional process in the production of a fermented beverage designated as "beer," "ale," "porter," "stout," "lager," or "malt liquor."</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu15" class="mmenu">
           FMB15 <a id="Q15" name="Q15"></a>: What are examples of non-traditional processes that require the filing of a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub15" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Removal of any volume of water from beer; filtration of beer to substantially change the color, flavor, or character; separation of beer into different components; reverse osmosis; concentration of beer; and ion exchange treatments are examples of non-traditional processes for which brewers must file a formula.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu16" class="mmenu">
           FMB16 <a id="Q16" name="Q16"></a>: What are examples of traditional processes for which no formula is required?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub16" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Pasteurization; filtration prior to bottling; filtration in lieu of pasteurization; centrifuging for clarity; lagering; carbonation; and blending are examples of traditional processes for which brewers do not have to file a formula.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu17" class="mmenu">
           FMB17 <a id="Q17" name="Q17"></a>: What should I do if I'm not sure whether the process used by my brewery requires the filing of a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub17" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The appropriate TTB officer may determine whether or not use of a process not listed in <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=0e0d6143502cbb948d782dbd368dd81a&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;rgn=div5#27:1.0.1.1.20.6.374.4" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR  25.55(a)(1)</a> requires you to file a formula for approval. You may obtain such a determination from TTB by mailing a written request to the Assistant Director, Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division, Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau, 1310 G Street, NW., Box 12 Washington, DC 20005.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu18" class="mmenu">
           FMB18 <a id="Q18" name="Q18"></a>: What information should be included in a request for a determination as to whether use of a process requires the filing of a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub18" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The request must include:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>A detailed description of the proposed process;</li> 
             <li>Evidence establishing that the proposed process is generally recognized as a traditional process in the production of a fermented beverage designated as "beer," "ale," "porter," "stout," "lager," or "malt liquor"; and</li> 
             <li>An explanation of the effect of the proposed process on the production of the fermented product.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu19" class="mmenu">
           FMB19 <a id="Q19" name="Q19"></a>: For what fermented products other than those produced through nontraditional processes must a formula be filed?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub19" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>In general, formulas must be filed for:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Any fermented product to which flavors or other nonbeverage ingredients (other than hop extract) containing alcohol will be added;</li> 
             <li>Any fermented product to which coloring or natural or artificial flavors will be added;</li> 
             <li>Any fermented product to which fruit, fruit juice, fruit concentrate, herbs, spices, honey, maple syrup, or other food materials will be added; and</li> 
             <li>Sak, including flavored sak and sparkling sak.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu20" class="mmenu">
           FMB20 <a id="Q20" name="Q20"></a>: Can I file for an exemption from the formula requirement for use of a particular coloring, flavoring, or food material?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub20" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. TTB will grant such an exemption upon a finding that the coloring, flavoring, or food material in question is generally recognized as a traditional ingredient in the production of a fermented beverage designated as "beer," "ale," "porter," "stout," "lager," or "malt liquor."</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu21" class="mmenu">
           FMB21 <a id="Q21" name="Q21"></a>: How do I file for such an exemption?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub21" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Your request should be sent to the Assistant Director, Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division, Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau, 1310 G Street, NW., Box 12 Washington, DC 20005, and must include the following information:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>A description of the proposed ingredient;</li> 
             <li>Evidence establishing that the proposed ingredient is generally recognized as a traditional ingredient in the production of a fermented beverage designated as "beer," "ale," "porter," "stout," "lager," or "malt liquor"; and</li> 
             <li>An explanation of the effect of the proposed ingredient in the production of a fermented product</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu22" class="mmenu">
           FMB22 <a id="Q22" name="Q22"></a>: What are the general requirements for filing a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub22" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The requirements are as follows:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>The formula must be filed in writing;</li> 
             <li>The formula must identify each brewery where the formula applies by including each brewery name, address, and registry number;</li> 
             <li>You must serially number each formula, commencing with number "1" and continuing in numerical sequence;</li> 
             <li>You must date and sign each formula; and</li> 
             <li>You must file two copies of each formula with TTB.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu23" class="mmenu">
           FMB23 <a id="Q23" name="Q23"></a>: Where do I file a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub23" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Your formula should be filed with the Assistant Director, Alcohol Labeling and Formulation Division, Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau, 1310 G Street, NW., Box 12 Washington, DC 20005.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu24" class="mmenu">
           FMB24 <a id="Q24" name="Q24"></a>: What information must appear on each formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub24" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The following information must appear on each formula:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>You must list each separate ingredient and the specific quantity used, or a range of quantities used.</li> 
             <li>You may include optional ingredients if they do not impact the labeling or identity of the finished product.</li> 
             <li>For fermented products containing flavorings, the following additional information must appear:</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p>The name of the flavor;</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>The product number or TTB drawback number and approval date of the flavor;</li> 
             <li>The name and location (city and State) of the flavor manufacturer;</li> 
             <li>The alcohol content of the flavor; and</li> 
             <li>The point of production at which the flavor was added (that is, before, during or after fermentation).</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p>For formulas that include the use of flavors and other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol, you must explicitly indicate:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>The volume and alcohol content of the beer base;</li> 
             <li>The maximum volumes of the flavors and other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol to be used;</li> 
             <li>The alcoholic strength of the flavors and other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol;</li> 
             <li>The overall alcohol contribution to the finished product provided by the addition of any flavors or other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol; and</li> 
             <li>The final volume and alcohol content of the finished product.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu25" class="mmenu">
           FMB25 <a id="Q25" name="Q25"></a>: If I received approval for a beer base formula, should that information be included in the formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub25" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. You must refer in your formula to any approved formula number that covers the production of a beer base used in producing the formula product. If the beer base was produced by another brewery of the same ownership, you must also provide the name and address or name and registry number of that brewery.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu26" class="mmenu">
           FMB26 <a id="Q26" name="Q26"></a>: What other requirements apply to all formulas?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub26" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The formula must also include a detailed description of each process used to produce the fermented beverage. The formula must state the alcohol content of the fermented product after fermentation and the alcohol content of the finished product. Finally, the appropriate TTB officer may at any time require you to file additional information regarding a fermented product, ingredients, or processes, in order to determine whether a formula should be approved or disapproved or whether the approval of a formula should be continued.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu27" class="mmenu">
           FMB27 <a id="Q27" name="Q27"></a>: If my formula includes flavors containing alcohol, am I required to list the alcohol contribution of individual flavors and other nonbeverage ingredients containing alcohol?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub27" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. However, you must state the total alcohol contribution from these ingredients to the finished product.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu28" class="mmenu">
           FMB28 <a id="Q28" name="Q28"></a>: When must I file a new formula (with a new formula number) for approval by TTB?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub28" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>A new formula must be filed when you </p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Create an entirely new fermented product that requires a formula;</li> 
             <li>Add new ingredients to an existing formulation;</li> 
             <li>Delete ingredients from an existing formulation;</li> 
             <li>Change the quantity of an ingredient used from the quantity or range of usage in an approved formula;</li> 
             <li>Change an approved processing, filtration, or other special method of manufacture that requires the filing of a formula; or</li> 
             <li>Change the contribution of alcohol from flavors or ingredients that contain alcohol.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu29" class="mmenu">
           FMB29 <a id="Q29" name="Q29"></a>: When may I file a superseding formula instead of a new formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub29" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You may file a superseding formula instead of a new formula if you change ingredients or processes and these changes would not require a new certificate of label approval. A superseding formula replaces an existing formula, and should be filed only if you do not intend to use the existing formula any more. A superseding formula must be filed with TTB for approval.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu30" class="mmenu">
           FMB30 <a id="Q30" name="Q30"></a>: How does a superseding formula affect the prior formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub30" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>When TTB approves a superseding formula, we will cancel your previous formula.</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu31" class="mmenu">
           FMB31 <a id="Q31" name="Q31"></a>: Should the superseding formula use the same formula number as the formula it replaces?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub31" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes, but you must annotate the formula number to indicate that it is a superseding formula number (For example, "Formula 2, superseding.")</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu32" class="mmenu">
           FMB32 <a id="Q32" name="Q32"></a>: Must separate formulas be filed for different products that require a formula?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub32" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu33" class="mmenu">
           FMB33 <a id="Q33" name="Q33"></a>: May I file a formula for a beer base to be used in the production of one or more other fermented products?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub33" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. The base must conform to the standards set forth in 27 CFR  25.15.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu34" class="mmenu">
           FMB34 <a id="Q34" name="Q34"></a>: When must a formula be filed?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub34" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>As a general rule, you may not produce a fermented product for which a formula is required until you have filed and received approval of a formula for that product.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu35" class="mmenu">
           FMB35 <a id="Q35" name="Q35"></a>: Is there an exception to the rule regarding prior approval of formulas?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub35" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You may, for research and development purposes (including consumer taste testing), produce a fermented product without an approved formula. However, if the product falls into the category of fermented products for which a formula is required, you may not sell or market the product until you receive approval of the formula.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu36" class="mmenu">
           FMB36 <a id="Q36" name="Q36"></a>: How long does my formula approval remain valid?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub36" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>As a general rule, your approved formula remains in effect until:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>you supsersede it with a new formula;</li> 
             <li>you voluntarily surrender the formula;</li> 
             <li>TTB cancels or revokes the formula; or</li> 
             <li>the formula is revoked by operation of law or regulation.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBmenu37" class="mmenu">
           FMB37 <a id="Q37" name="Q37"></a>: Will statements of process that were approved prior to the effective date of TTB TD-21 remain valid on and after January 3, 2006?
          </div> 
          <div id="FMBsub37" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes, provided that any finished product that could be made under the statement of process would be in compliance with the provisions <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=0e0d6143502cbb948d782dbd368dd81a&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;rgn=div5">27 CFR part 25</a>, as amended by <a href="http://www.gpo.gov/fdsys/pkg/FR-2005-01-03/pdf/04-28460.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">TTB TD-21</a>. You do not need to submit a new formula for approval if the product is covered by a statement of process that remains valid.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_caffeine" class="print_caffeine">
          <a id="caffeine" name="caffeine"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_caffeine')" href="#caffeine"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine</h3> 
          <div id="CABmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab1" name="cab1"></a>CAB1: What Actions Has FDA Taken with Regard to Malt Beverages Containing Added Caffeine?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>By letter dated November 17, 2010, FDA advised four industry members that it had reviewed the regulatory status of seven malt beverage products, each of which contains caffeine that has been directly added to an alcohol beverage and packaged in combined caffeine and alcohol form. The FDA letter warned the industry members that as it was used in their products, caffeine is an unsafe food additive, and therefore the products are adulterated under section 402(a)(2)(C) of the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (FFDCA), 21 U.S.C. 342(a)(2)(C). Among other things, the FDA letter stated that "FDA is not aware of any publicly available data to establish affirmatively safe conditions of use for caffeine added directly to alcoholic beverages and packaged in a combined form."</p> 
            <p>FDA provided these industry members with fifteen (15) days to advise them of the specific steps they have taken to correct the violation identified above and to assure that similar violations do not occur. The FDA letter provided that their responses should include any documentation necessary to show that correction has been achieved. Finally, the FDA letter provided that if the industry members cannot complete all corrections within the 15 days, they should explain the reason for the delay and the date by which each such item will be corrected and documented. The warning letters, as well as other information on the issue of alcohol beverage products containing added caffeine, may be found on the <a href="https://www.fda.gov/food/ingredientspackaginglabeling/default.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">FDA website</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/20/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab2" name="cab2"></a>CAB2: What Actions Has TTB Taken With Regard to the Malt Beverages Identified by FDA as Adulterated?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>On November 18, 2010, TTB issued letters to those four industry members regarding the seven malt beverage products that FDA identified in its warning letters as being adulterated. The TTB letters put these companies on notice that FDA's determination that a product is adulterated under the FFDCA would have consequences under the FAA Act, because of TTB's position that adulterated alcohol beverages are mislabeled within the meaning of the FAA Act.</p> 
            <p>Consistent with the terms of the FDA warning letters, TTB asked that the companies advise TTB within the same 15-day period of the steps that they have taken to correct any violations of the FAA Act and the date by which each violation will be corrected. TTB sent copies of these letters to the brewers who have obtained certificates of label approval from TTB for these products. You can read the TTB letters, along with other TTB guidance on the issue of <a href="/main-pages/caffiene-added">alcohol beverage products containing added caffeine</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab3" name="cab3"></a>CAB3: Will TTB Take Enforcement Action with Regard to the Alcohol Beverages that FDA Has Identified as Adulterated?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Consistent with the actions taken by FDA, TTB is not planning to take enforcement action pending expiration of the 15-day period provided to the companies to respond to our letters. At that point, we will evaluate their responses and we will consult with FDA prior to taking enforcement action. It is our expectation that the companies will take voluntary action that will prevent any violations of the FAA Act and will at the same time address the concerns expressed by FDA.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab4" name="cab4"></a>CAB4: What are the Consequences under the FAA Act of a Determination that an Alcohol Beverage Product is Adulterated?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>It is TTB's position that adulterated malt beverages, distilled spirits, and wines are mislabeled within the meaning of the FAA Act. This means, as explained further below, that the sale or shipment of an adulterated alcohol beverage in interstate or foreign commerce by an industry member subject to the provisions of <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=83623&amp;SIZE=21170&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 205(e)</a> constitutes a violation of the FAA Act, even if the bottler or importer of the product in question has obtained a certificate of label approval (COLA) or an approved formula.</p> 
            <p>Subject to the jurisdictional requirements of the FAA Act, mislabeled distilled spirits, wines, and malt beverages, including adulterated products, may not be sold or shipped, delivered for sale or shipment, or otherwise introduced or received in interstate or foreign commerce, or removed from customs custody for consumption, by a producer, importer, or wholesaler, or other industry member subject to <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=83623&amp;SIZE=21170&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 205(e)</a>. TTB may pursue action to suspend or to revoke the FAA Act basic permit of industry members who willfully violate the conditions of their permit with respect to mislabeled, adulterated products. See <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=72288&amp;SIZE=11329&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 204(e)</a>. Violations of the labeling provisions of the FAA Act are punishable as misdemeanors and the Government may seek injunctive relief to prevent and restrain such violations. TTB also may seek an offer in compromise covering the liability arising with respect to such violations in the sum of not more than $500 for each offense. See <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=107848&amp;SIZE=4960&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 207</a>. Under the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, TTB officers may, in appropriate circumstances, temporarily detain any alcohol beverage container that is being removed in violation of law, or seek a voluntary detention agreement with the industry member. See <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc26.wais&amp;start=19872015&amp;SIZE=1944&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">26 U.S.C. 5311</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab5" name="cab5"></a>CAB5: What if I Have Obtained a COLA or Formula Approval for My Alcohol Beverage?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>TTB reminds you that each producer and importer of alcohol beverages is responsible for ensuring that the ingredients in its products comply with the laws and regulations that FDA administers. TTB's approval of a COLA or formula does not imply or otherwise constitute a determination that the product complies with the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (FFD&amp;CA), including a determination as to whether the product is adulterated because it contains an unapproved food additive. Subject to the jurisdictional requirements of the FAA Act, mislabeled distilled spirits, wines, and malt beverages, including adulterated products, may not be sold or shipped, delivered for sale or shipment, or otherwise introduced or received in interstate or foreign commerce, or removed from customs custody for consumption, by a producer, importer, or wholesaler, or other industry member subject to 27 U.S.C. 205(e), even if the bottler or importer of the product in question has obtained a COLA or an approved formula.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu6" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab6" name="cab6"></a>CAB6: How do TTB and FDA Interact with Regard to Adulterated Alcohol Beverages?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>While TTB regulates the labeling of alcohol beverages pursuant to the FAA Act, it is FDA's responsibility to evaluate the safety of ingredients added to alcohol beverages, pursuant to FDA's authority under the FFDCA. TTB operates under a <a href="/main-pages/memo-of-understanding">1987 Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) with FDA</a> that clarifies and delineates the enforcement responsibilities of each agency with respect to alcohol beverages that may be adulterated under the FFDCA and establishes procedures for coordination between the two agencies. The MOU acknowledges that TTB is the agency with a system of specific statutory and regulatory controls over alcohol beverages and that FDA has authority regarding determinations regarding the safety of food additives used in the production of alcohol beverages and over making determinations about when an alcohol beverage is considered adulterated.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu7" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab7" name="cab7"></a>CAB7: Is TTB Sharing Information with FDA About Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. TTB will continue to coordinate with FDA on this matter that affects issues within the jurisdiction of both agencies. TTB has already shared information with FDA regarding approved labels for alcohol beverages containing added caffeine, and we will continue to do so, as needed. In addition, upon receipt of a formal request from FDA, we will provide information to FDA about formulas for beers containing added caffeine that are approved under <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=ab7ad4d824f8ff8390ea2f035ba43158&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.20&amp;idno=27" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR Part 25</a>. This disclosure will be made pursuant to our authority under <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc26.wais&amp;start=21221927&amp;SIZE=259305&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">26 U.S.C. 6103(o)(1)</a> to share return information with employees of a Federal agency whose official duties require such disclosure. Such a disclosure is contingent upon an agreement by FDA to safeguard the confidentiality of this information.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu8" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab8" name="cab8"></a>CAB8: Will TTB Continue to Approve Labels or Formulas for Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>TTB urges all industry members to carefully consider their responsibilities to comply with the requirements of the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (FFD&amp;CA) and to consult with FDA regarding the <a href="https://www.fda.gov/food/ingredientspackaginglabeling/gras/default.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">General Recognized As Safe (GRAS)</a> status of their intended use of caffeine prior to submitting any such applications to TTB.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu9" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab9" name="cab9"></a>CAB9: Will TTB Take Action with Regard to Approved Labels or Formulas for Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub9" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>TTB is reviewing all approved formulas and labels for such products and will consult with FDA prior to taking action with regard to approved labels or formulas. We encourage all industry members who have received approvals from TTB and who have reason to believe that their products may not be in compliance with the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (FFD&amp;CA).</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu10" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab10" name="cab10"></a>CAB10: Does the Return of Alcohol Beverages Containing Added Caffeine by a Retailer or Wholesaler Violate the FAA Act's Prohibitions Against Consignment Sales?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub10" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. Among other things, the FAA Act's prohibitions against consignment sales apply only to the conditions agreed to at the time of a sale. Furthermore, these prohibitions do not apply to transactions involving solely the bona fide return of merchandise for ordinary and usual commercial reasons arising after the merchandise has been sold. See <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=83623&amp;SIZE=21170&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 205(d)</a>. The regulations at <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=ab7ad4d824f8ff8390ea2f035ba43158&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.9&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.9.4" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR Part 11, Subpart D</a> set forth several examples of "ordinary and usual commercial reasons" that may arise after the product has been sold, including a situation in which products may no longer be lawfully sold. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=ab7ad4d824f8ff8390ea2f035ba43158&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.9&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.9.4.43.4" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 11.34</a>. The actions of a retailer or wholesaler in returning to an industry member alcohol beverages containing added caffeine, after the sale of the product, for cash or credit against outstanding indebtedness, due to concerns about the legal status of such products under Federal, State, or local law, would not violate the consignment sales provisions of <a href="http://frwebgate.access.gpo.gov/cgi-bin/usc.cgi?ACTION=RETRIEVE&amp;FILE=%24%24xa%24%24busc27.wais&amp;start=83623&amp;SIZE=21170&amp;TYPE=TEXT" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 U.S.C. 205(d)</a>. Of course, the regulations do not mandate that the industry member accept such a return. See <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr&amp;sid=ab7ad4d824f8ff8390ea2f035ba43158&amp;rgn=div5&amp;view=text&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.9&amp;idno=27#27:1.0.1.1.9.4.43.1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">27 CFR 11.31(b)</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/19/2012</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="CABmenu11" class="mmenu">
           <a id="cab11" name="cab11"></a>CAB11: What if My Alcohol Beverage Product Contains Caffeine But I Did Not Receive a Warning Letter from FDA?
          </div> 
          <div id="CABsub11" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Industry members should contact FDA with all inquiries as to the GRAS* status of ingredients added to alcohol beverages. TTB will continue to coordinate with FDA on this matter.</p> 
            <p><a href="https://www.fda.gov/food/ingredientspackaginglabeling/gras/default.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">* generally recognized as safe</a></p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p>
