         <div id="print_ecp" class="print_ecp">
          <a id="ecp" name="ecp"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_ecp')" href="#ecp"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Export Certificate Program</h3> 
          <div id="ECPmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp1" name="ecp1"></a>ECP1: How do I obtain an Export Certificate for wines, malt beverages, or distilled spirits being shipped to a foreign country?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <p>You can find information about the Export Certificate Program on TTB's webpage for <a href="/itd/export-documents-certificates">Export Documents/Certificates</a>. For Certificates of Free Sale, Origin, Health, Quality, or Sanitation, for shipments of alcohol beverages <em>not</em> going to the European Union (EU), follow the <a href="/images/itd/docs/sample-certificate-of-free-sale-wine.doc">sample export certificate for wines</a> or the <a href="/images/itd/docs/sample-certificate-of-free-sale-for-spirits.doc">sample export certificate for malt beverages and distilled spirits</a>. For U.S. wine being exported to the EU, pursuant to the U.S.-EU Wine Agreement, the EU requires that you submit either a <a href="/images/industry_circulars/archives/2007/attachment09-02.pdf" target="_blank">simplified export certificate</a> (<a href="#ecp5">see ECP5</a>) or a VI1 form.</p> 
           <p>Please email export certificate requests as PDF files to <a href="mailto:exportcertificates@ttb.gov">exportcertificates@ttb.gov</a></p> 
           <p>You may also mail export certificate requests to the following address:</p> 
           <p>Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau (TTB) <br> International Affairs Division<br> Attn: Export Certificate Program<br> 1310 G St. NW, Box 12<br> Washington, DC 20005</p> 
           <p>If you are submitting your export certificate requests through a commercial carrier (e.g. UPS, FedEx), please mail them to:</p> Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau (TTB) 
           <br> International Affairs Division
           <br> Attn: Export Certificate Program
           <br> 1310 G St. NW, Suite 400E
           <br> Washington, DC 20005 
           <p><strong>For distilled spirits only: </strong></p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Use <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f511058.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Form 5110.58 </a>to make requests for Certificates of Age and Origin for Distilled Spirits.</li> 
            <li>Use <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f511042.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Form 5110.42 </a>to make requests for Certificates of Authenticity for Bourbon Whisky. You may submit Certificates of Age and Origin and Certificates of Authenticity via email to <a href="mailto:exportcertificates@ttb.gov">exportcertificates@ttb.gov</a> (See <a href="#ecp7">ECP7</a>).</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 08/05/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp2" name="ecp2"></a>ECP2: How much time will it take for me to obtain an export certificate?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Our goal is to process export certificates within seven business days after receipt of a perfected request. In order to avoid delays, you may choose to submit your requests using a commercial carrier by overnight delivery. Please note that due to internal mail security measures, items mailed to TTB Headquarters are typically received by the International Affairs Division two business days after indicated by delivery confirmations from the postal service or a commercial carrier. To expedite the return of approved certificates, please include an overnight bill and envelope from the commercial carrier of your choice, including your own billing/account information when you submit your request to TTB. Otherwise, TTB will return the certificate via regular U.S. mail.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/12/2013</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp3" name="ecp3"></a>ECP3: Does each label of wine need an individual Certificate of Origin or Age or Health Certificate/Sanitary Statement/Certificate?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Each shipment of wine that is being exported requires a separate export certificate (Certificate of Origin or Age, Health Certificate/Sanitary Statement/Certificate, etc.). One certificate can cover several different wines as long as they are in the same shipment.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/12/2013</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp4" name="ecp4"></a>ECP4: I am not familiar with the Certificate of Free Sale and Certificate of Authenticity. Are they licenses?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Export certificates are not licenses - they are documents that attest to certain facts. For example, a Certificate of Free Sale confirms that the wine being exported was made in accordance with U.S. winemaking practices and is freely available in the U.S. marketplace. Certificates of Origin are also often referred to as Certificates of Free Sale.</p> 
            <p>A number of countries have unique certificate requirements. TTB maintains a list of <a href="/itd/international-imports-exports-requirements">International Import/Export Requirements</a> on our website; however, countries may change their requirements at any time, so we recommend that you contact your foreign importer to confirm which certificates are required by that country's government.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/12/2013</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp5" name="ecp5"></a>ECP5: I am exporting wine to the European Union. Must I use a VI1 for the exportation of wine products?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Instead of using the VI1 form, we encourage U.S. exporters of wine to the EU to take advantage of the simplified export certificate, which only requires one chemical analysis of the wine (actual alcohol content) and is self-certified by the exporter.</p> 
            <p>See <a href="/images/industry_circulars/archives/2007/07-02.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">TTB Industry Circular 2007-02</a> for further information on the simplified export certificate. A copy of the certificate is included in Industry Circular 2007-2 as an attachment at the bottom of that document.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/12/2013</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu6" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp6" name="ecp6"></a>ECP6: I need a chemical analysis of the product. Where can I find a list of approved laboratories?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You can find a list of laboratories certified by TTB for the analysis of exported alcohol products on our<a href="/scientific-services-division/chemist-certification-program"> Chemist Certification Program Information</a> webpage.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu7" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp7" name="ecp7"></a>ECP7: Can I submit requests for export certificates electronically?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You may submit export certificates by email as PDF files to <a href="mailto:exportcertificates@ttb.gov">exportcertificates@ttb.gov</a>. If you require return of the certificate by express mail, you must scan in a prepared overnight bill from the commercial carrier of your choice, including your own billing/account information, and attach it to your email request. Otherwise, TTB will return the certificate by regular U.S. mail.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu8" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp8" name="ecp8"></a>ECP8: Can my local Chamber of Commerce process export certificates for me?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes, your local Chamber of Commerce may process Certificates of Origin attesting that the alcohol beverage to be exported was produced in the United States.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 12/12/2013</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPmenu9" class="mmenu">
           <a id="ecp9" name="ecp9"></a>ECP9: What can I do to ensure that my export certificates will be processed by TTB as quickly as possible?
          </div> 
          <div id="ECPsub9" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You can help us process your export certificate request expeditiously by following these tips:</p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Except for Certificates of Origin and Age of Distilled Spirits and Certificates of Authenticity for Bourbon Whiskey, TTB requires that the export certificate include an original signature. We recommend that the name of the person signing the document be typed after or below their signature, in case the signature is not legible.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <ul> 
             <li>The person signing the export certificate request must be on file with TTB as having signing authority for the company or having power of attorney for the company. We cannot process an export certificate if it is not signed by someone with signing authority or power of attorney.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Submit the export certificate on your company's letterhead. TTB requires that the physical address listed on your company's letterhead, or on the export certificate, match the address on file with your permit with TTB.<br><br></li> 
             <li>We recommend that you send in one copy of the export certificate on your company's letterhead plus an additional copy of the export certificate on plain paper, with space at the top and bottom of the page for TTB to insert our official letterhead. TTB requires that both copies contain an original signature.<br><br></li> 
             <li>Use TTB's Washington, DC address when you include it on the export certificate. Some industry members are still including TTB's Cincinnati address. This slows down processing time because we will replace this address with our current address in order to process it. If you include TTB's address at the bottom of the export certificate, use this address: <br><br> Alcohol and Tobacco Tax and Trade Bureau (TTB) <br> International Affairs Division<br> Export Certificate Program<br> 1310 G St. NW, Box 12<br> Washington, DC 20005</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div>

         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_sf" class="print_sf">
          <a id="sf" name="sf"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_sf')" href="#sf"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Serving Facts Statements</h3> 
          <p><a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>, Voluntary Nutrient Content Statements in the Labeling and Advertising of Wines, Distilled Spirits, and Malt Beverages</p> 
          <div id="SFmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf1" name="sf1"></a>SF1: What is the effect of TTB Ruling 2013-2?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <p>This ruling modifies and amplifies <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> to permit the use of optional Serving Facts statements on labels and in advertisements.</p> 
           <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
           <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf2" name="sf2"></a>SF2: Is the use of a Serving Facts statement mandatory or optional?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>It is optional. You may use a Serving Facts statement on any label or advertisement, and you may choose to use a Serving Facts statement in lieu of a statement of average analysis when making calorie or carbohydrate claims on labels or in advertisements. See question 4 for additional information about using a Serving Facts statement on labels with calorie or carbohydrate claims.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf3" name="sf3"></a>SF3: May I use a Serving Facts statement or a statement of average analysis on a label or in an advertisement that does not make any other calorie or carbohydrate claims?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf4" name="sf4"></a>SF4: May I make a low-calorie claim on a label that does not include either a statement of average analysis or a Serving Facts statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. It has been the longstanding position of TTB and its predecessor agency that any caloric or carbohydrate statement or representation in the labeling and advertising of wines, distilled spirits, and malt beverages will be viewed as misleading unless it provides complete information about the calorie, carbohydrate, protein, and fat content of the product. As set forth in <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a>, a statement of average analysis, which includes information about calories, carbohydrates, protein and fat content on a per-serving basis, ensured that such labels or advertisements did not mislead consumers.</p> 
            <p><a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a> does not change that position. Instead, it offers industry members an additional option in providing consumers with information about the nutrient and alcohol content of the product. TTB will view labels and advertisements as misleading if they make claims about the calorie or carbohydrate content of the product unless they include either a statement of average analysis in accordance with TTB Ruling 2004-1 or a Serving Facts statement that complies with the requirements of TTB Ruling 2013-2. Thus, a Serving Facts statement may now be used on such labels instead of a statement of average analysis.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf5" name="sf5"></a>SF5: I've been using a statement of average analysis on my "light" beer labels for years. May I continue to do so?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. Statements of average analysis that comply with the requirements of <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> may continue to be used on labels and in advertisements.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu6" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf6" name="sf6"></a>SF6: What is a Serving Facts statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>A Serving Facts statement includes the serving size, the number of servings per container, and the number of calories and the number of grams of carbohydrates, protein, and fat, per serving size. In addition, you may choose to include the percentage of alcohol by volume in the statement, and if you do so, you may also include the number of fluid ounces of pure ethyl alcohol per serving as part of the alcohol by volume statement.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu7" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf7" name="sf7"></a>SF7: May I use a Serving Facts statement on a keg?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. The labeling provisions of TTB Rulings <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">2013-2</a> and<a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank"> 2004-1</a> apply to all containers used for the sale of wines, distilled spirits, or malt beverages at retail, including kegs.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu8" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf8" name="sf8"></a>SF8: My malt beverages have a brand name that includes the term "light." However, in my advertisements, I make no other claims about nutrients (such as calories, carbohydrates, protein or fat). Am I required to place a Serving Facts statement or a statement of average analysis on these advertisements?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. If your advertisement does not make any other claim about the nutrient content of the product, you are not required to place a Serving Facts statement or a statement of average analysis on the advertisement. However, labels for products including terms such as "light" in their brand names will not be approved without a statement of average analysis or a Serving Facts statement, unless the term "light" is used in a way that clearly does not refer to nutrient content.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu9" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf9" name="sf9"></a>SF9: If I wish to place a Serving Facts statement on my label or in my advertisement, should I provide information based on a serving or on the entire container?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub9" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>A Serving Facts statement appearing on a label or in an advertisement may be stated per container size only if the container is equal to or less than a single serving size. However, as an option, the Serving Facts statement may be presented in a dual-column format, which provides information both per serving size and per container size.</p> 
            <p>Otherwise, the Serving Facts statement must be stated per serving size, and must specify the serving size as part of the statement. Serving sizes for purposes of Serving Facts labeling are specified in the chart below. These serving sizes must also be used when calculating the number of servings per container, which should be rounded to the nearest quarter of a serving. For example, a malt beverage with an alcohol content of 5 percent alcohol by volume in a can that contains 16 fl.oz. should be labeled as containing 1  12 fl.oz. servings.</p> 
            <table style="width: 800px;" border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="3" align="center">

               <td style="width: 432px;" colspan="3"> <p>Alcohol Percent by Volume</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p>Wine</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Distilled Spirits</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Malt Beverages</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>1.5 fl oz (44 ml), or 50 ml for 50 ml containers of distilled spirits</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 138px;">&nbsp;</td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 24%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 24%</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>2.5 fl oz (74 ml)</p> </td>

            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu10" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf10" name="sf10"></a>SF10: Do I need to submit a new application for label approval if the only change to my label is to include either a Serving Facts statement or a statement of average analysis?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub10" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>If an approved label is being changed only to include a statement of average analysis in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> or a Serving Facts statement in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>, and the format for the Serving Facts statement is one that is depicted in the examples provided in the attachment to TTB Ruling 2013-2, the submission of a new application for a certificate of label approval (COLA) is not necessary.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu11" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf11" name="sf11"></a>SF11: Do I need to submit a new application for label approval if my approved label includes a statement of average analysis, but I want to remove that statement and replace it with a Serving Facts statement in one of the formats set out in the attachment to TTB Ruling 2013-2?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub11" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No. You may make that change without submitting a new application for label approval.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu12" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf12" name="sf12"></a>SF12: May I add a Serving Facts statement to my approved label and also make additional changes without submitting a new application for label approval?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub12" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You may add a Serving Facts statement to your approved label as permitted in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>, and you may also make additional changes as permitted in accordance with the instructions for the COLA application form, <a href="/images/pdfs/forms/f510031.pdf" target="_blank">TTB F 5100.31</a> (which also appear on COLAs Online for electronic submitters), without having to submit a new application for label approval. If the additional changes are not covered by the instructions on the COLA application form, you must submit a new application for label approval. Get a complete list of allowable changes and learn more about <a href="/news/allowable-changes-label-generator">what changes can be made to an approved label</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu13" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf13" name="sf13"></a>SF13: Am I required to use a panel for the Serving Facts statement, or may I present this information in a linear display?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub13" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The attachment to <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a> provides examples of both a panel display and a linear display. You may choose whichever display fits best on your label or advertisement.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu14" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf14" name="sf14"></a>SF14: May I include a Serving Facts statement on my label in a format that is different from the examples set forth in TTB Ruling 2013-2?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub14" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You must submit a new application for label approval if you wish to use a format that differs from the examples set forth in the attachment to<a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank"> TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>. Other formats for this type of information will be considered on a case-by-case basis. In considering other formats, TTB will take into consideration whether a proliferation of formats might tend to confuse consumers.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu15" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf15" name="sf15"></a>SF15: May I include a Serving Facts statement on my label or in my advertisement without including information about the alcohol content of the product in the Serving Facts statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub15" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. Serving Facts statements may include information about the alcohol content of the product on an optional basis. However, industry members may choose to not include alcohol content in the Serving Facts statement. An example of this format is set out in the attachment to <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu16" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf16" name="sf16"></a>SF16: May I include the percentage of alcohol by volume on my Serving Facts statement without including a statement of the fluid ounces of alcohol per serving?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub16" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. Alcohol content may be presented in the Serving Facts statement as a percentage of alcohol by volume. In addition, if alcohol content is expressed as a percentage of alcohol by volume, the Serving Facts statement may also include a statement of the fluid ounces of pure ethyl alcohol per serving (rounded to the nearest tenth) as part of the alcohol by volume statement. However, industry members may choose to include the percentage of alcohol by volume in the Serving Facts statement without including a statement of the number of fluid ounces of alcohol per serving.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu17" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf17" name="sf17"></a>SF17: The regulations require that certain products must include an alcohol content statement on the brand label. If I include an optional alcohol content statement as part of a Serving Facts statement for such products on a label other than the brand label, am I required to repeat the alcohol content statement on the brand label?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub17" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. The inclusion of an optional alcohol content statement as part of a Serving Facts statement does not excuse industry members from compliance with existing regulations regarding the placement of mandatory alcohol content statements. The regulations require an alcohol content statement on the brand label for all distilled spirits and for those malt beverages containing alcohol derived from added flavors or other added nonbeverage ingredients (other than hops extract) containing alcohol. However, alcohol content statements may appear in more than one place on the container, provided that they are consistent and in compliance with all regulatory requirements. The percentage of alcohol by volume for wine containers may appear on any label.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu18" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf18" name="sf18"></a>SF18: I would like to add a Serving Facts statement to my approved label without submitting a new COLA application. May I use abbreviations for the terms used in the optional Serving Facts statement, or must I use the exact terms set forth in the examples?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub18" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The following abbreviations may be used on labels and in advertisements bearing the optional Serving Facts statement, with or without periods after the abbreviations:</p> 
            <p style="padding-left: 30px;">(1) For "Alcohol by volume," the abbreviations "Alc/vol" or "Alc by vol"; <br> (2) For U.S. fluid ounces, "fl oz"; <br> (3) For calories, "Cal"; <br> (4) For grams, "g"; <br> (5) For Carbohydrate, "Carb"; <br> (6) For serving (except in the title "Serving Facts"), "Serv";<br> (7) For milliliter, "ml"; and <br> (8) For amount, "Amt."</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu19" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf19" name="sf19"></a>SF19: May I place the optional Serving Facts statement on my product's neck label?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub19" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>You may include the optional Serving Facts statement on any label on the container, including a strip or neck label.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SFmenu20" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sf20" name="sf20"></a>SF20: Are there type size or font requirements for Serving Facts statements?
          </div> 
          <div id="SFsub20" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>There are no specific type size or font requirements for the optional Serving Facts statement on labels or in advertisements. However, the statement should be on a contrasting background and should be readily legible under ordinary circumstances.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 01/02/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_sug" class="print_sug">
          <a id="sug" name="sug"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_sug')" href="#sug"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Sugar Content Statements</h3> 
          <div id="SUGmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sug1" name="sug1"></a>SUG1: May I provide information about the number of grams, per serving, of sugar in my product on my label or in my advertisement?
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Truthful, accurate, and non-misleading numerical statements about the sugar content of a product are permitted on alcohol beverage labels and in advertisements. Sugar is a type of carbohydrate, so a sugar content statement is a carbohydrate claim and must be made in accordance with the guidance set forth for carbohydrate representations in <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> and <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>. Accordingly, a truthful, accurate, and non-misleading numerical statement about the sugar content of a product may appear on a label or in an advertisement if the label or advertisement also bears either a statement of average analysis in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> or a Serving Facts statement in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a> and the serving size on which the sugar content statement is based is consistent with the applicable serving size under those rulings.</p> 
            <p>Numerical sugar content claims should be made in accordance with the guidance set forth in <a href="/images/pdfs/2004_1_rulling_carbohydrate_calc.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Procedure 2004-1</a> with regard to carbohydrate content statements. Thus, the number of grams (g) of sugar in a serving must be expressed to the nearest tenth of a gram, except that if a serving contains less than 1 gram, the statement "Contains less than 1 gram (g)" or "less than 1 gram (g)" may be used as an alternative. If the serving contains less than 0.5 g of sugar, the content may be expressed as zero (or 0) grams (g).</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/01/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sug2" name="sug2"></a>SUG2: May my label or advertisement include a claim such as "Zero Sugar," "No Sugar," or "Sugar Free," if the product contains less than 0.5 g of sugar per serving?
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGsub2" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes, if a serving contains less than 0.5 g of sugar, you may include a claim such as "Zero Sugar," "No Sugar," or "Sugar Free." Such claims must be made in accordance with the guidance set forth for carbohydrate representations in <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> and <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>, which provides that the label or advertisement must also include either a statement of average analysis in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2004-1.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2004-1</a> or a Serving Facts statement in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>. The serving size on which the sugar content statement is based must be consistent with the applicable serving size under those rulings.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/01/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sug3" name="sug3"></a>SUG3: What is meant by sugars on an alcohol beverage label or advertisement?
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>For purpose of this guidance, the term "sugars" refers to the sum of free monosaccharides and disaccharides in the beverage. To calculate sugars, you must determine the weight in grams per serving of all free monosaccharides and disaccharides in the beverage sample. Do not include any artificial or natural no-calorie sweeteners in your calculation.</p> 
            <p>TTB generally monitors compliance of labeling and advertising claims by using appropriate methods found in the Official Methods of Analysis of the AOAC International (AOAC International, Gaithersburg, MD).</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/01/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sug4" name="sug4"></a>SUG4: Does this guidance apply to labeling claims indicating a higher sugar content for the grapes used in wine that are made in accordance with ATF Ruling 82-4 and ATF Ruling 78-4?
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>This guidance does not apply to wine labels bearing a descriptive term (such as "Late Harvest") that is intended to indicate a higher sugar content for the grapes used in the wine. TTB allows the use of certain descriptive terms relating to the sugar content of grapes provided that the amount of sugar contained in the grapes at the time of harvest and the amount of residual sugar in the finished wine are stated on the label, in compliance with the provisions of <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/78-4.htm" target="_blank">ATF Ruling 78-4</a> and <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/82-4.htm">ATF Ruling 82-4</a>. Such statements are not required to be accompanied by a statement of average analysis or a Serving Facts statement, and you should refer to <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/78-4.htm" target="_blank">ATF Ruling 78-4</a> and <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/82-4.htm">ATF Ruling 82-4</a> for guidance on use of this type of statement.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/01/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="sug5" name="sug5"></a>SUG5: May I include health claims on labels and advertisements suggesting that my sugar-free alcohol beverage is appropriate for persons suffering from certain diseases or health-related conditions?
          </div> 
          <div id="SUGsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>TTB reminds industry members that due to the health risks posed by alcohol consumption, sugar content is not the only factor in determining whether an alcohol beverage is appropriate for consumption by persons suffering from health-related conditions. Statements, symbols, vignettes, or other forms of labeling or advertising statements that expressly, or by implication, characterize the relationship of the product, or the sugar content of the product, to a disease or health-related condition are prohibited unless such statements comply with the requirements for specific health claims as set forth in the TTB regulations. See 27 CFR <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.2.4.25.12&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">4.39(h)(2)(ii)</a>,<a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.2.7.25.5&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">4.64(i)(2)(ii)</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.3.5.25.15&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">5.42(b)(8)(ii)(B)</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.3.9.25.5&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">5.65(d)(2)(ii)</a>, <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.5.3.41.12&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">7.29(e)(2)(ii)</a>, and <a href="http://www.ecfr.gov/cgi-bin/text-idx?SID=3dbf27a1d0d9a60c0c21e8ef62727f09&amp;node=27:1.0.1.1.5.6.41.5&amp;rgn=div8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">7.54(e)(2)(ii)</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 07/01/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
         <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         <div id="print_af" class="print_af">
          <a id="af" name="af"></a> 
          <p id="printIcon" class="printIcon" align="right"><a onclick="printContent('print_af')" href="#af"><img src="/images/printer.gif" alt="Print" width="24" height="24" align="top" border="0" hspace="4">Print</a></p> 
          <h3>Alcohol Facts Statements</h3> 
          <div id="AFmenu1" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af1" name="af1"></a>AF1: May I provide per-serving alcohol content information on my label or in my advertisement without providing nutrient content information?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub1" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Yes. If your label or advertisement does not include any nutrient content statements or claims, you may provide the same truthful and accurate per-serving alcohol content information that is allowed as part of a Serving Facts statement under <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>. This information should be provided under the heading "Alcohol Facts," to distinguish it from a "Serving Facts" statement, and must include the serving size (in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>), the number of servings per container, and the percentage of alcohol by volume together with a numerical statement of the number of fluid ounces of pure ethyl alcohol per serving (rounded to the nearest tenth). If you wish to make any type of nutrient content statement or claim on the label or advertisement, along with optional per-serving alcohol content information, you should use a Serving Facts statement in accordance with <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu2" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af2" name="af2"></a>AF2: What serving sizes must I use if I include an Alcohol Facts statement on my label or in my advertisement?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub2" class="subMenu" style="height: 440px;"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Serving sizes for purposes of Alcohol Facts labeling must be consistent with the sizes set forth in <a href="/images/pdfs/rulings/2013-2.pdf" target="_blank">TTB Ruling 2013-2</a>, and are specified in the chart below.</p> 
            <table style="width: 100%;" border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="5" align="left"> 
             <tbody> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;" rowspan="2"> <p align="center">Serving Size</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 432px;" colspan="3"> <p align="center">Alcohol Percent by Volume</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p align="center">Wine</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p align="center">Distilled Spirits</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p align="center">Malt Beverages</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>1.5 fl oz (44 ml), or 50 ml for 50 ml containers of distilled spirits</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p>&nbsp;</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 24%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>&nbsp;Above 24%</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>2.5 fl oz (74 ml)</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p>Above 16 to 24%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 16 to 24%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 16 to 24%</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>5 fl oz (148 ml)</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p>7 to 16%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 7 to 16%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Above 7 to 16%</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td style="width: 150px;"> <p>12 fl oz (355 ml)</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 138px;"> <p>&nbsp;</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Not more than 7%</p> </td> 
               <td style="width: 147px;"> <p>Not more than 7%</p> </td> 
              </tr> 
             </tbody> 
            </table> 
            <p>&nbsp;</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu3" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af3" name="af3"></a>AF3: How do I calculate the number of servings per container?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub3" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The number of servings per container is calculated by dividing the total net contents by the serving size as specified by <strong>AF2</strong>. The number of servings in a container must be rounded to the nearest quarter of a serving. Examples of determining the number of servings per container are shown below.</p> 
            <p><strong><em>16 fluid ounce can of beer at 12 percent alcohol by volume:</em></strong></p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Alc. by vol.: 12%</li> 
             <li>Total net contents: &nbsp;16 fl. oz.</li> 
             <li>Serving size: &nbsp;5 fl. oz.</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Servings per container</span>: &nbsp;16 fl. oz.  5 fl. oz. = 3.20 rounded to the nearest quarter of a serving = <strong>3&nbsp;1/4</strong> servings per container.</p> 
            <p><strong><em>1 liter bottle of distilled spirits at 40 percent alcohol by volume</em></strong></p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Alc. by vol.: 40%</li> 
             <li>Total net contents: 1 Liter (1000 ml)</li> 
             <li>Serving size: &nbsp;1.5 fl. oz. (44 ml)</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Servings per container</span>: &nbsp;1000 ml  44 ml = 22.73 rounded to the nearest quarter of a serving =<strong> 22 3/4</strong> servings per container</p> 
            <p><strong><em>750 ml bottle of wine at 13.5 percent alcohol by volume</em></strong></p> 
            <ul> 
             <li>Alc. by vol. 13.5%</li> 
             <li>Total net contents: 750 ml</li> 
             <li>Serving size: 5 fl. oz. (148 ml)</li> 
            </ul> 
            <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Servings per container</span>: &nbsp;750 ml  148 ml = 5.07 rounded to the nearest quarter of a serving = <strong>5</strong> servings per container</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/07/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu4" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af4" name="af4"></a>AF4: How do I calculate the fluid ounces of alcohol per serving?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub4" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The number of fluid ounces of alcohol per serving is calculated by multiplying the number of fluid ounces in a serving by the percentage of alcohol by volume and rounding to the nearest tenth of a fluid ounce. Examples are set forth below:</p> 
            <p><em>Wine at 14 percent alcohol by volume</em><br><em>Serving size: </em>&nbsp;<strong>5 fl. oz.</strong> &nbsp;<em>Alcohol by volume:</em> &nbsp;<strong>14% (or 0.14)</strong><br><em>Fl. &nbsp;oz. of alcohol per serving:</em> &nbsp;<strong>5 x 0.14 = 0.7 fl. oz. of alcohol per serving</strong></p> 
            <p><em>Malt beverage at 4 percent alcohol by volume</em><br><em>Serving size:</em> &nbsp;<strong>12 fl. oz.</strong> &nbsp;<em>Alcohol by volume:</em> &nbsp;<strong>4% (or 0.04)</strong><br><em>Fl. &nbsp;oz. of alcohol per serving: </em>&nbsp;<strong>12 x 0.04 = 0.48 fl. oz. of alcohol per serving (rounded to 0.5)</strong></p> 
            <p><em>Distilled spirits at 40 percent alcohol by volume</em><br><em>Serving size: </em>&nbsp;<strong>1.5 fl. oz.</strong> &nbsp;<em>Alcohol by volume:</em> &nbsp;<strong>40% (or 0.4)</strong><br><em>Fl. oz. of alcohol per serving:</em> &nbsp;<strong>1.5 x 0.4 = 0.6 fl. oz. of alcohol per serving</strong></p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu5" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af5" name="af5"></a>AF5: May the "Alcohol Facts" statement be stated per container size?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub5" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>An Alcohol Facts statement appearing on a label or an advertisement may be stated per container size only if the container size is equal to or less than a single serving size. However, as an option, the Alcohol Facts statement may be presented in a format that provides information both per serving size and per container size.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu6" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af6" name="af6"></a>AF6: Is there a minimum type size for Alcohol Facts statements?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub6" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Generally, there are no minimum type size requirements for Alcohol Facts statements; however, the information should be readily legible and appear on a contrasting background. If it is being used to satisfy an alcohol content statement requirement on labels or in advertisements, it must meet the type size and placement requirements for that information.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu7" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af7" name="af7"></a>AF7: Does the inclusion of an "Alcohol Facts" statement on my label satisfy any applicable regulatory requirements for an alcohol content statement?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub7" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>The TTB <a href="/labeling/laws-and-regulations">labeling regulations</a> require an alcohol content statement, expressed as a percentage of alcohol by volume, for certain products. Because the Alcohol Facts statement includes a statement of the percentage of alcohol by volume, it will satisfy those requirements as long as it complies with the placement and type size requirements set forth in the regulations.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 06/10/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div id="AFmenu8" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af8" name="af8"></a>AF8: Must I submit a new application for label approval if I want to add an "Alcohol Facts" statement to my approved label?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub8" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>No, if an approved label is being changed only to include an Alcohol Facts statement following the guidelines in these FAQs, and the format used is one that is depicted in the examples provided in AF9, the submission of a new application for label approval is not necessary.</p> 
            <p><span class="crumbs">Last reviewed/updated 05/06/2014</span></p> 
            <p><a href="#content">Return to Top</a></p> 
           </div> 
          </div>

          <div id="AFmenu10" class="mmenu">
           <a id="af10"></a>AF10: Will TTB consider other formats for Alcohol Facts information?
          </div> 
          <div id="AFsub10" class="subMenu"> 
           <div class="subs"> 
            <p>Other formats for per-serving alcohol content information will be considered on a case-by-case basis and will necessitate the submission of a new COLA application.</p>
